Tangshan Coal Mine Labor Strike: Mediation Gradually Shows Promise

Tangshan Gentry and Business Representatives Confer at the Commissioner's Office

Decided to First Advance 11,000 Yuan for Bereavement Payments

Then Negotiate Resumption Conditions with the Mining Bureau

The Mining Bureau's Attitude is Exceptionally Firm

Tianjin Japanese Consul General Met with Yu Xuezhong Regarding This Labor Strike

(Tianjin) On the 4th, at 9 PM, Tao Shangming invited Zhao Xun, the factory representative of the Industrial Office, Li Yinchun, and Tangshan gentry and businessmen to a meeting at the Commissioner's Office to discuss solutions to the labor strike. The meeting adjourned at 12 AM without any results. On the 4th, Tao Shangming telephoned the Kailuan Mining Bureau in Tianjin, urging them to quickly send representatives to negotiate terms. The mining company insisted on an unconditional resumption of work and refused to send anyone. On the 4th, around 11 PM, Tangshan miners planned to surround the Commissioner's Office again, demanding that their conditions be met. Tao Shangming urgently sent people to stop them, telling them that he was trying to find a solution and urging them not to surround and disturb again. The workers demanded a final response by noon on the 5th, and all actions were prepared. If the mining company did not send anyone by noon on the 5th, they would take effective action. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) On the 5th, striking Tangshan miners did not make any statements. He Zi'en, a member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, fearing that the deadlock would lead the workers to extremes and affect the market, joined forces with President Sun of Tangshan Jiaotong University, Zhou, the manager of the Bank of Communications, gentlemen Liu Jinping, Liu Xigui, and others, in the capacity of a third party, to discuss matters with Tao Shangming, Zhao Xun, and worker representatives. Because the strike had lasted for a long time and their livelihoods were difficult, the workers were unwilling to listen to Zhao Dazhong's commands and sincerely hoped that the mining company would allow reasonable conditions for them to resume work. Therefore, He and others came forward to mediate, and the situation was quite promising. Tao Shangming, Zhao Xun, and Tangshan gentry held a meeting at the Commissioner's Office on the 5th and decided that the local government should first advance 11,000 yuan to pay compensation for worker injuries and deaths, to ease the labor unrest, and then negotiate terms with the mining company, so that the workers could resume work as soon as possible. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) On the 5th, at 3 PM, the Japanese Consul General in Tianjin, Zhai Lansi, visited Yu Xuezhong at the Hebei Provincial Government regarding the Kailuan Coal Mine labor strike. They talked for a long time. The British side wanted the provincial government to forcefully suppress the workers and arrest Zhao Dazhong, who was instigating the labor unrest. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Kailuan Mining Bureau successively submitted reports to the Hebei Provincial Government on the 3rd and 4th. (1) "This afternoon, the Mining Bureau received a phone call from Commissioner Tao saying that the leader of the Tangshan disturbance, Zhao Dazhong, claimed at the Commissioner's Office that if the Mining Bureau did not immediately agree to the two demands of increasing wages and paying all workers who did not work during the riots, then the workers would rush into the mine factory at 6 PM today, destroy the radio station, stop the water pumps, and flood the mine shafts, etc. The Mining Bureau has been fully aware of all the circumstances of the frequent riots in various mining areas recently. If there are problems between labor and capital, they should be raised in accordance with the procedures stipulated by the Factory Law. Why should they repeatedly use riotous behavior to pressure the capitalists, endanger lives and property, and disregard national laws, social order, and security? Moreover, Zhao Dazhong is not a worker, so how can he participate? This is even more bizarre. Under these circumstances, the Mining Bureau will never give in. In addition to requesting Commissioner Tao to protect lives and property at the time, it is reasonable to report to Your Excellency. We humbly request you to preside over and protect the lives and property within the Mining Bureau and mining areas." (2) (Above omitted) "The Mining Bureau has not complied with the legal procedures at all in the recent labor unrest. Without any warning to the capitalists, it immediately resorted to riots, endangering lives, damaging property, intimidating good workers, preventing them from going to work, and openly firing guns at disobedient workers, surrounding government offices, intimidating administrative officials and the Mining Bureau, and disregarding the government, disrupting order, which is tantamount to treason. The punishment they deserve seems to be more severe than that stipulated by the laws concerning ordinary labor-capital disputes; otherwise, national laws will lose their effectiveness, local security will not be maintained, and people's lives, property, and rights to be enjoyed within the scope of the law will not be guaranteed. Urgent words, we humbly ask Your Excellency to examine and preside over." (5th Dispatch)

Anti-Japanese Volunteers in Mishan Battle the Enemy

(Harbin) Since March 30th, the Tanaka Detachment, together with the puppet army, has been attacking the anti-Japanese volunteers north of Mishan. Fierce battles have lasted for several days, and both sides have suffered losses. The Japanese claim that one Japanese soldier was killed and one wounded. (5th Hualian Dispatch)

He Yingqin Agrees to Become Chief Administrator of Inner Mongolia's Autonomous Government

Yesterday's Banquet for High-Ranking Military and Political Figures in Beiping

(Beiping) After Huang Shaohong's persuasion, He Yingqin has agreed to take the position of Chief Administrator to guide the autonomy of Inner Mongolia. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) He Yingqin hosted a banquet at Jurentang tonight for North China generals and political figures in Beiping. Those invited included Wan Fulin, Shang Zhen, Wang Shuchang, Jiang Bocheng, Ji Qiao, Fu Zhan Kui, Bao Wen Yue, He Qi Gong, Yuan Liang, Yu Jin, Yin Rugeng, and more than twenty others. (5th Dispatch)

Puppet Police in Gubeikou Demand Withdrawal Fee

Using Reimbursement of Huge Housing Repair Costs as a Condition for Withdrawal

Yin Rugeng Negotiates with the Japanese Side

Chai Shan Telegraphed Songjing for Consultation

Japanese Emperor's Aide-de-Camp, Machijiri, Arrives in Beiping

(Tianjin) Regarding the puppet police in Caojia Road, Gubeikou demanding a huge withdrawal fee, Yin Rugeng is negotiating with the Japanese side. Chai Shan will go on the 6th to investigate the situation and then decide whether to withdraw. The provincial government allocated 10,000 yuan for the installation of long-distance telephone lines between Yutian, Zunhua, Malanyu, Gubeikou, and Tongpingjin. Construction started on the 5th and will be completed in two weeks. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng will not go to Beiping for the time being due to certain matters. Negotiations for the takeover of Malanyu will first be held with Chai Shan in Beiping. Implementation will be scheduled after progress is made. The political power there is originally in our hands, but the issue of the withdrawal of Japanese and puppet troops is the focus of the handover. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Machijiri Teiki, the Japanese Emperor's aide-de-camp who was ordered to comfort the Japanese troops stationed in North China, arrived in Beiping from Tianjin this afternoon. Accompanying him were Chief of Staff Zhu Chi and eight military officers. They are scheduled to inspect Gubeikou on the 6th, return to Beiping on the 7th, and go to Luandong on the 8th for inspection. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) After we formally took over Gubeikou, the puppet border police team stationed there has delayed its withdrawal to this day. They stated to our side that the repair costs for the Caojia Roadkou and Nantianguan Beishanyin resident posts amounted to more than 920 yuan, and the repair costs for the puppet police headquarters in Nanguan, Gubeikou, amounted to more than 19,000 yuan. Only after our side reimburses them will they be able to find other houses and relocate. Our authorities believe that such a request is extremely difficult to fulfill in reality, and have repeatedly negotiated with the Japanese authorities, hoping for an early resolution. Japanese military officer Chai Shan has telegraphed Matsui, the head of the Kwantung Army Special Affairs Agency in Chengde, inviting him to go to Gubeikou on the 6th to discuss specific measures for the withdrawal of the puppet police. Yin Rugeng originally planned to attend, but due to official business in Tianjin, he has sent Huo Shi, director of the Gubeikou Office, as his representative. The future relocation site of the puppet police may be in Bakeshi Camp. (5th Dispatch)

Japanese Intrusion and Survey Plans

Military and Political

(Beiping) The situation in eastern Chahar is still very tense. It is said that the Japanese side has made two preparations for intrusion and surveying: first, military, and they are currently building airfields and motor roads in eastern Chahar; second, political, and they will induce eastern Mongolia to undermine Mongolian autonomy. (5th Dispatch)

Japanese Troops Conduct Exercises and Marches in the Tianjin Southern Saltwater Area

(Tianjin) At 7:30 AM on the 5th, two battalions of Japanese troops in Tianjin went to the saltwater area south of Tianjin by truck to conduct marching exercises, all the way to Tanggu. Our side specifically notified the public not to panic excessively. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The commander of the Japanese troops stationed in Tianjin, Meijiro Umezu, visited Yu Xuezhong at the Provincial Government on the 5th. (5th Dispatch)

Yin Rugeng Receives Funds to Reorganize and Dismiss the Yutian Special Police

Severe Alert Inside Yutian City

Preventing Reorganized Police from Causing Disturbances

(Tianjin) The dismissal fee for the Yutian special police is issued according to 900 people, 10 yuan per person. After the funds are issued, they are not allowed to stay in the county and will be escorted back to their hometowns. The provincial government ordered transportation agencies to exempt them from road fees. Yin Rugeng has received the funds and will return to Beiping this afternoon at 4 PM and send someone to assist Han Dianbang in handling the matter. The provincial government received a report that sandbags were piled up at the gates of Yutian City because Captain Han feared that the reorganized police would escape and disrupt the area, so he took severe precautions. The Yutian Security Team is organized into two battalions and two special teams, each battalion with three companies, plus the two special teams, for a total of eight companies. Feng Shoushan was appointed as the captain of the special team, but he is unwilling and wants to expand it into a large battalion. The provincial government holds Yin Rugeng and Han Dianbang responsible for handling this matter. It is rumored that Feng Shoushan secretly came to Tianjin and is active in a certain concession, but after investigation, this is not true. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) On the morning of the 4th, the Yutian Security Team suddenly piled sacks on the city gates, created defensive works, and the team soldiers were armed and alert, strictly checking entry and exit. The opening and closing of the city gates were at fixed times, and no entry or exit was allowed after the time was up. The electric lights, telephone, and telegraph bureau in the county town were all guarded by team police. The long-distance telephone line was cut again. The county people were alarmed, rumors arose again, and merchants closed their doors early. The people of Ya Hongqiao Town, fearing a second military disaster, fled in droves. The provincial government has not yet received a report from the county magistrate about this matter today. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng went to the Hebei Provincial Government this morning to visit Yu Xuezhong and discuss the Yutian incident again. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yin Rugeng went to Tianjin earlier to negotiate with various parties on matters such as the reduction of salaries for the Yutian Security Team and the takeover of Malanyu. He returned to Beiping tonight after completing the matters. It is said that Yin's trip to Tianjin was successful and he plans to return to Tongzhou tomorrow morning and then go to Yutian. After a short stay, he will go to Malanyu to meet with Captain Jian Gong, the Japanese garrison, to discuss everything. (5th Dispatch)

Remnants of Liu's Bandits Raid Dadian Town

Shandong Troops Return to Suppress and Exterminate Them

Gan Yu County Town Has Been Recovered

(Jinan) Han Fuju said that when the remnants of Liu's bandits left Shandong, there were only two or three hundred people. After breaking through Gan Yu, they colluded with local bandits and grew to five or six hundred people. Tonight, they suddenly raided south of Dadian Town, fifty miles south of Ju County, on the border between Jiangsu and Shandong. Fortunately, the returning provincial troops were on their way, making deployment convenient. He has ordered the two brigades of Li Xiangchen and Ning Chunxiao to rush back to Dadian to intercept them, and also ordered the division commanders Sun Tongxuan and Gu Liangmin to return from Jiangsu Province to encircle and attack. The Ma Guan Yi brigade is also advancing towards Dadian. All troops can arrive by car tonight. After the bandits broke through Gan Yu, many people were killed, and corpses lined the roads. (5th Dispatch)

(Zhenjiang) Gan Yu County Town was recovered at noon on the 4th. The remaining bandits retreated to the Huanbu Dun area. County Magistrate Chuan Zhiren has returned to the city to handle the aftermath. According to Director Xiang of the Security Department, Liu's bandits are in the appearance of fleeing famine towards Pi County. The provincial government is currently sending troops to prevent and block them. (5th Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) The Third Army Headquarters received a telegram from Brigade Commander Li from the front line, stating that 2,000 remnants of Liu's bandits raided Gan Yu County Town on the 4th. On the 5th, the pursuing troops of the Shandong Army arrived, and the bandits fled to Shahe Town. Our army urgently advanced and launched a fierce attack. The bandits then fled towards Huandun. We are currently cooperating with the Shandong Army in encircling and suppressing them. The coastal defense is strict, and the road defense is solid. (5th Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) According to road news, Liu's bandits fled south from Gan Yu and were attacked by the 7th Division in Shahe on the 5th. They retreated to Huandun on the border between Jiangsu and Shandong. The 7th Division's troops are rushing forward to pursue and attack, and the Shandong Army is also following up to cooperate in the suppression. The coastal defense is strict, and the road defense is firm. (5th Dispatch)

Yang Monkey's Remaining Bandits are Being Surrounded and Suppressed in Wuchuan

Sun Dianying Will Come to Beiping Later

Men Bingyue Returns to Beiping to Report

(Beiping) A telegram from Baotou states that Men Bingyue returned to Beiping this morning to report on his mission and will arrive on the 6th. Yang Monkey's remaining bandits, numbering more than six hundred, fled to Wuchuan and have been surrounded by three regiments of the Jin-Sui Army. (5th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Liu Zengruo, Secretary-General of Sun Dianying, telegraphed from Taiyuan to Beiping today, stating that He's letter to Sun has been forwarded. Sun stated that he would come to Beiping after finishing his personal affairs in Taiyuan. Liu telegraphed to Beiping, hoping that the authorities would cancel Sun's position as a member of the Military Branch Committee. (5th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Fu Zuoyi telegraphed to President Wang, stating that Sun's troops have been closely deployed between San Sheng Gong and Dengkou, using both coercion and inducement. They have been surrendering one after another in recent days. Today, they have all turned in their weapons, leaving not a single gun or bullet. They have all become unarmed and are being sent to the rear in succession. Except for Yang Monkey, a bandit chief with a thousand followers on the border between Sui and Ningxia, who fled into the mountains, our infantry, cavalry, and artillery joint force has been ordered to fiercely suppress him and has already annihilated four or five hundred bandits and captured his chief of staff, Nan Jingchen. The search and suppression is still actively underway. Countless guns and goods seized at the front are being inventoried by Division Commander Wang Jingguo and Men Bingyue, a senior staff officer. The bandit troops have been thoroughly resolved. This is respectfully reported by telegram. (5th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Ma Hongkui's representative, Bai Jianmin, came to Tianjin from Beiping on the 4th to entertain the press. According to him, Chairman Ma has been unable to extricate himself from the reorganization of military and political affairs and the aftermath, but he has decided to come to Beiping in person recently to report everything to the two chairmen, He and Huang. Sun Dianying's troops have been reorganized by various parties, but Yang Monkey's remaining six hundred men are still unwilling to submit and are fleeing east and west. The provincial army is searching and suppressing them and will soon be able to eliminate them. Although Ningxia is nominally a province, it only has eight counties. Since Sun's troops caused disturbances, the province has not received any tax revenue for two months, and the treasury is empty. Therefore, post-disaster relief is urgently needed, waiting for the 50,000 yuan allocated by the central government. At present, there is a lack of food for the people, and transportation in various places has not been restored, making it very difficult to transport supplies from other provinces. The worst affected are Pingluo and Dengkou, while Ningxia is lighter. Yu Ximing's troops have all surrendered their weapons. Ding Futing and Liu Yueting live in Ningxia and will be given other appointments by Chairman Ma in the future. Li Chunhua and Lu Chunyi's troops have recently received orders from the central government to go to Gansu for garrison. (4th Dispatch)

Provincial Bandit Suppression Troops Ordered to Converge on Tongnan

The Third Phase of the General Offensive Begins

(Hankou) On the 3rd, the Sichuan bandit suppression army began the third phase of the general offensive, breaking through Xu's bandits' strong fortifications and occupying Yiankou Chang, Shilong Chang, Shiguan Yin, Sha Niu Ping, Zhao Jia Ping, and other places. Liu Xiang ordered the various armies to converge on Tongnan to complete the third phase of the plan. (5th Dispatch)

Victory News from the Nanchang Headquarters

Rumors of Luo Bingyao's Death in Battle

(Nanchang) The headquarters announced that after the Fourth Division recovered Xinqiao in Tai Ning, the bandits, using the false Third Army Corps, the Fourth and Fifth Divisions, the false Fifth Army Corps, the Thirteenth Division, and the false Ninth Army Corps, the Thirty-fourth Division, with more than 30,000 men, continuously attacked from the 25th to the 27th. Finally, our forces, fighting bravely and taking the lead, killed 2,000 bandits. There are rumors that Luo Binghui, a bandit leader, was killed in battle. The bandits are extremely short of morale and supplies and are easily defeated in battle. (4th Dispatch)

(Nanchang) The headquarters received a telegram from Yu Hanmou on the 26th, stating that the false 22nd Division attacked the communist annihilation regiment stationed in Tianxin Xu. The Li Division advanced to suppress them and encountered the bandit vanguard in Wu Long, engaging in a fierce battle all day, killing and wounding 200 bandits and capturing 70 guns. They are still following up. Also, Pei Division telegraphed on the 26th that they encountered the false 28th Army in Hongshiyan, engaging in a fierce battle all day, killing hundreds of bandits. The remaining bandits fled towards Badao He. (5th Dispatch)

The Eastern Route Army is Rushing to Build the Western Fujian Highway

Contact Has Been Made with the Guangdong Army

Limit of Ten Days to Recover Liancheng

(Xiamen) According to news from Longyan, the Third Division advanced to Lao Wu Hui Fengting to construct a highway. The 83rd Division occupied Da Cen Xia Taiping Xu to cover the road-building troops. The 9th Division's 26th Brigade guarded Longyan, and the 25th Brigade advanced to Wai Chi to build roads. The Guangdong Army's 29th arrived at Da Ban Tu Chi and made contact with the Third Division. (5th Dispatch)

(Xiamen) After You Sifu was detained in Yongchun, more than 100 of his troops surrendered their weapons. You is a major bandit in southern Fujian, and the province offered a reward of 10,000 yuan for his capture. (5th Dispatch)

(Xiamen) The Eastern Route Headquarters notified the newspapers not to publish Jiang Dingwen's movements. (5th Dispatch)

(Fuzhou) The Eastern Route Army's divisions are attacking Liancheng, with a limit of ten days to recover it, in order to jointly attack the Changding Pengkou area. The battles have been fierce in recent days. The bandits are internally chaotic and will be difficult to sustain. The Military Commission sent Guo Diancheng to Fujian to handle transportation matters at the front. (5th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Fuzhou) The Min Army's Liu Chaoran's Security Office was reorganized into the 13th Security Regiment and ordered to be transferred to Minqing, under the command of the Eastern District Branch. (5th Dispatch)

(Fuzhou) The National Army in Jianning has been engaging in fierce battles with the bandits for days and has been victorious. The vanguard is only tens of miles away from Jiancheng. Tang Enbo personally went to the front to command, and the entire bandit line has been shaken. (5th Dispatch)

Imperialists' Conspiracy in Tibet

An Article in the Russian Pravda

(Moscow) Pravda published an article titled "Imperialists' Conspiracy in Tibet," stating, "The Exchange Telegraph Agency reported that a Tibetan delegation visited the Panchen Lama, urging him to enter Tibet. The agency also predicted that the civil war in Tibet is becoming increasingly mature. Since leaving Tibet, the Panchen has turned to serve Japanese imperialism in order to extend the latter's tentacles to Tibet, thereby threatening British interests." The newspaper pointed out that Tibet is the most important part of British imperialism's policy of plundering colonies. The British have established a military group and army in Tibet and are using their army to advance their military actions in China. This military action did not cease until the Dalai Lama's death and has recently been revived. British imperialism has turned "Greater Tibet" into "Lesser Tibet" by nibbling away at the outer edge of the land and is now working to expand it at the expense of other parts of China's territory, while using the soup from Tibet to aid its swallowing of these territories. Therefore, its opposition to the Panchen's return to Tibet is only natural." (4th Tass Dispatch)

Yunnan Military Officer Reports on the Evolution of Yunnan-Burma Boundary Affairs

Chiang Kai-shek Summons Li Yuankai to Jiangxi for Consultation

(Nanjing) Zhao Yunan, a Yunnan military officer, came to Beijing in response to a telegram from the Yunnan Native Association in Beijing. He visited He Yaotu, the counselor, on the morning of the 5th to report on the evolution of Yunnan-Burma boundary affairs. (5th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) A certain member of the border affairs group of the General Staff Department said that the authorities attached great importance after the Pan Hong incident and ordered Huang Musong to invite Yunnan representatives to discuss and study it. After several meetings, it was decided to request the central government to select Li Yuankai and Yang Guangcan, Yunnan province staff members from this department, as the main and deputy experts, to work with commissioners sent by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and senior surveyors from the Army Survey Bureau, to conduct surveys, set up accurate markers, and notify the British to send representatives to go together to implement the boundary, to solve this major dispute as soon as possible. Chiang Kai-shek, to clarify the situation, has telegraphed Li Yuankai to Jiangxi to consult on everything and give instructions on survey matters. Li will return to Beijing within days. Whether Chiang Kai-shek will send him there will be decided upon his return to Beijing. (5th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Chu Minyi said that the Executive Yuan had not yet received a reply from the Yunnan Provincial Government regarding the rumor of British troops invading Lancang. (5th Dispatch)

Sino-Turkish Friendship Treaty Signed in Turkish Capital

Our Representative is Hu Weide

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, the Sino-Turkish Friendship Treaty was signed in the Turkish capital on the 4th. Negotiations on the treaty began in 1930 and took nearly four years of back-and-forth discussions before being signed on the 4th of this month. After ratification by the two governments, a commercial treaty will be negotiated. Although it is still too early to talk about sending ministers to each other, the authorities of both countries are already searching and considering candidates. (5th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) For the sake of enhancing friendly relations between the Chinese and Turkish governments, both sides previously sent representatives to negotiate a treaty. However, due to various reasons, negotiations went back and forth for several years without any agreement. Recently, because Minister to Switzerland Hu Shize was going to Egypt to attend the Universal Postal Congress, our Ministry of Foreign Affairs instructed Minister Hu to go to Ankara, the capital of Turkey, to directly negotiate and sign a treaty with the Turkish Foreign Minister. According to a telegram from Minister Hu, the Sino-Turkish Friendship Treaty has been negotiated and signed with the Turkish Foreign Minister in the Turkish capital on April 4th. The treaty simply stipulates that the two countries will mutually send diplomatic representatives to enjoy the treatment recognized by the usual principles of international law. After the treaty is ratified by the two governments, the instruments of ratification will be exchanged in Geneva within days. Also, Turkish Foreign Minister Rastou telegraphed our Minister of Foreign Affairs Wang, expressing congratulations, and Wang replied with a telegram of thanks on the 5th. The two telegrams are as follows: (1) Telegram to Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing: I am extremely pleased to inform you that I have signed the Sino-Turkish Friendship Treaty with Minister Hu. I also take this opportunity to express to Your Excellency that I sincerely hope that the inherent friendly relations between China and Turkey will become even more developed. (2) Reply telegram to the Minister of Foreign Affairs in Ankara: I am grateful for your telegram of the 4th. I would like to express to Your Excellency that I am equally pleased with the conclusion of the Sino-Turkish Friendship Treaty, and it is foreseeable that the inherent friendly relations between China and Turkey will be further consolidated by this treaty. (5th Central News Agency Dispatch)

No Reply Received from the British Side Regarding the Revision of the Sino-British Commercial Treaty

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, no reply has yet been received from the British side regarding the revision of the Sino-British Commercial Treaty. However, the most important point of the revision is the recovery of inland river navigation rights. Although the abolition of extraterritoriality is important, the British side may consider it less important than navigation rights. Our government has collected various materials for reference when conducting negotiations. (5th Dispatch)

Resolutions of the Central Standing Committee Meeting

Build a National Assembly Hall in the Capital

(Nanjing) The Central Committee held its 115th Standing Committee meeting at 8 a.m. on the 5th, attended by more than 20 people, including Wang Zhaoming, Sun Ke, and Ju Zheng. Wang Zhaoming chaired the meeting, and the resolutions were as follows: (1) All Party Affairs Guidance Committee members in Henan Province will be transferred back, and Hong Ludong will be appointed as the special commissioner for Party affairs in the province, responsible for presiding over Party affairs in the province. A design committee will be established to plan various implementation plans. (2) Wang Jingxuan and Guo Yingfu will be added as Party Affairs Guidance Committee members for Shaanxi Province. (3) Approved the organizational regulations for the Book and Magazine Review Committee. (4) Party headquarters at all provincial, county, and city levels should jointly hold Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week with the government. (5) A National Assembly Hall will be built in the capital to serve as a temporary venue for the National Assembly. Kong Xiangxi, Ye Chucang, Tang Youren, Chu Minyi, Gan Naiguang, Fu Rulin, and Shi Ying will be appointed as members of the Construction Committee, with Kong Xiangxi designated as the convener to plan the name, funding, location, and all construction equipment, and to supervise the Nanjing Municipal Government to expedite the construction. (6) Chen Lifu will report on the April 12th Purification Movement Memorial. (7) Zhang Ji will report at the Central Memorial Week next Monday. (8) Other proposals. (5th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Huang Shaoxiong Arrives in Taiyuan

(Taiyuan) Minister of Interior Huang Shaoxiong arrived in Taiyuan at 6 p.m. on the 5th. Xu, Zhao, and others went to the station to welcome him. After Huang got off the train and greeted the welcomers, he went to the Sui Administration with Zhao and others to attend a welcoming banquet. Huang brought six followers, all of whom stayed at the Shanxi Grand Hotel. He is scheduled to meet with Yan Xishan at the riverbank tomorrow morning and inspect the construction situation in Shanxi Province, and will stay for about a week before going to Suiyuan. (5th Dispatch)

Huang Fu Passes Through Hankou to Jiangxi

Tang Youren Travels East on the Same Ship

(Hankou) Huang Fu arrived in Hankou at 10:00 AM on the 5th via train from Peiping. He boarded the Dehe steamer in the evening to go to Jiangxi. Huang stated that many locations along the Huangtan and Changcheng lines have already been taken over, and negotiations are underway for those that have not. The proposal for through trains and postal services, previously raised, has been stalled due to differing opinions. North China is currently peaceful. Sun Dianying's troops have been reorganized, and the reorganization of the Yutian security force is also proceeding smoothly. The situation is generally optimistic. Tang Youren traveled east on the same ship as Huang in the evening. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) On the 5th in Hankou, Huang Fu visited Zhang Xueliang and Zhang Qun for discussions. He then traveled to Jiangxi in the evening to meet with Chiang Kai-shek to discuss North China diplomacy. He will stay in Jiangxi for four days before going to Nanjing to see Wang Jingwei, then returning to Zhejiang to sweep his ancestral graves. The date of his return north is yet to be determined. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Before his departure, Huang Fu said that Japan's increased troop deployment in eastern Chahar will inevitably affect Inner Mongolia. However, the Bailingmiao Autonomous Council has been scheduled to be established, which is sufficient to respond to the situation. He has ordered relevant authorities to guard against Japan's recruitment of Chinese laborers. There is no need to expand the Peiping Political Reorganization Committee; rumors to the contrary are inaccurate. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Tang Youren stated that the situation in North China is not only serious diplomatically, but also complex in various other aspects. In the future, we must improve domestic governance to adequately respond to the situation. After persuasion, Shi Ying has agreed to return to Nanjing within days. (5th Special Dispatch)

Control Yuan Members Advocate Expanding Powers

(Nanjing) Members of the Control Yuan advocate expanding the powers of the Control Yuan regarding the section on its powers in the draft constitution. In addition to the power of impeachment, they believe it should also have the powers of questioning, disciplinary action, and making suggestions. Several principles have been decided, and Liu Eqing has been chosen to draft a proposal, which will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for reference after being discussed and approved at the next plenary meeting. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Chu Minyi stated that the special commissioners inspection methods announced by the Executive Yuan differ in nature from the supervising envoys of the Control Yuan. The Executive Yuan has not yet received the inquiry proposed by the Control Yuan as reported in the newspapers. (5th Special Dispatch)

President Wang Orders Investigation into Groups Damaging Clothing

(Nanjing) President Wang telegraphed the Ministry of Interior, the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and the Peiping Political Reorganization Committee on the 5th, stating: "Reading newspaper reports, it is said that there are so-called 'destruction groups' in Hangzhou, Peiping, and other places, specializing in cutting and damaging Western-style clothes, and that Nanjing is also about to initiate such activities. Please investigate whether this is true. The Capital Police Department and the Public Security Bureau should be ordered to take concrete preventative measures and conduct strict investigations. It should be understood that such actions are childish and reckless, making us a laughingstock to the world. Furthermore, domestic woolen fabrics are a new emerging industry, and the government should actively promote and protect them, giving them the same importance as domestic silk and native cloth. If these people are allowed to run rampant under this pretext, it will not only infringe on the freedom and protection of the people's bodies and property, but also stifle the budding of new industries, which is unacceptable under the law. Moreover, today the army, navy, and air force personnel all wear uniforms, which are also so-called Western suits. In the eyes of these people, they should also be included in the destruction list. Is this not wanting the army, navy, and air force personnel to wear long gowns and mandarin jackets to the battlefield? Furthermore, our country, in view of its weakness, is promoting militarization. If everyone must wear long gowns and mandarin jackets, is this not the height of contradiction? Promoting domestic goods is indeed an urgent task, but we should also diligently persuade people to use domestic silk and cloth when wearing long gowns and mandarin jackets, and domestic woolen fabrics when wearing Western suits. If they act irrationally and presumptuously, they will be liable to violating the police regulations at the very least, and the criminal law at the most. Those responsible for maintaining public safety must not sit idly by and allow this to happen, lest they incur blame. Please comply accordingly." (5th Special Dispatch)

Current Commentary

Reliance, Evasion, and Researching Japan's Court

The Chinese people have always suffered from the common ailment of dependency. Before the Northeast was completely lost, we relied on the policy of non-resistance. Immediately after the loss, we relied on the League of Nations and the United States to come to our defense. Unexpectedly, the League of Nations proved ineffective and the United States was too cautious. So, we hoped to rely on the Soviet Union and Japan to engage in all-out war. Diplomatic avenues were not entirely smooth, so we also hoped for internal disturbances within Japan, hoping they would have an unprecedented revolution. Because if Japan were to truly have a revolution, it would naturally be too busy to take care of itself. Then, recovering the Northeast would be as easy as turning one's hand. As for whether such a lucky and convenient thing would happen, we could just leave it to fate.

However, regardless, those infected with the disease of reliance will never forget the goals they hope for. In other words, the Chinese people, while holding onto the extravagant hopes that the League of Nations, the United States, and Russia would provide assistance from the sidelines and that Japan would have a revolution, still wanted to recover the four eastern provinces. Now, it seems that the symptoms have become even more dangerous. Because most people believe that relying on various parties offers little hope. But if we don't rely on them, we can't see a way out. Therefore, the disease of reliance has transformed into the disease of evasion. You evade, saying you won't do it. I evade, saying you are incompetent. Fortunately, national affairs are everyone's responsibility. If you don't do your best, how can you blame me? Thus, everyone goes their own way, seeking their own peace. The people's spirit within the country gradually goes from vigorous to indifferent, and from indifferent to frozen. It's a pity that the fate of tens of millions of compatriots is entrusted to the four eastern provinces, but in the minds of the general public within the customs, I fear that there is not much deep impression left.

Recently, I heard that a very small number of people among the intellectual class, perhaps because their self-awareness is particularly sharp and the suffering they feel is particularly profound, have been forced to fight alone, diligently researching Japanese economic and scientific journals, trying to guess their psychology. It seems that they are not satisfied with merely fulfilling their initial intellectual desires and considering the matter closed. The Japanese believe that this kind of research has profound implications, and is not merely a superficial phenomenon. The focus is also on this. However, it is not necessary to discuss how effective it is for a very small number of people wielding pens to attempt to single-handedly shoulder the heavy burden of national survival, while also having to rely on materials from the enemy to seek thorough understanding. But their arduous efforts are enough to make us sigh incessantly.

Since the September 18th Incident, the vast majority of people in the country have gone from reliance to evasion, and from evasion to living in comfort. The facts are there, and there is no denying it. Now, what we hope for from the people and the government is, first, to quickly cure the diseases of evasion and reliance, to clearly admit our own errors, and not to pray to gods and ghosts, or to complain about heaven and blame others. In particular, the government should guide everyone to do the work of "knowing that it cannot be done, but doing it anyway." Head-on research of Japan is one method of doing this kind of work.

Speaking of researching Japan, it is somewhat different from ordinary academic research. We must have a preconceived notion in our minds. We must not be intimidated by the various superficial advances of Japan as a result of our research. We must know that while Japan is indeed much stronger than China, it still inevitably lags behind when competing with Europe and the United States. The more we research Japan, the more we must restore our national self-confidence, and the more we must eliminate the inferior roots of reliance and evasion. There are many people in the country now who have studied in Japan. Some of them, perhaps because they understand the great principle of "knowing yourself and knowing your enemy" too thoroughly, have the model of Japan as something amazing deeply embedded in their minds, and are unwilling to easily smash it. Too much is as bad as too little, and they also urgently need to be improved.

Some people say that in these extraordinary times amidst national disaster, the atmosphere is so stifling that they don't even want to speak. It's better to research some Japanese or Soviet problems to find some solace. They don't know that using research as solace is like using escapist Zen as transcendence. It's equally useless, and equally unable to escape the circle of reliance and evasion. If we unfortunately reach this point, we must also find a way to correct it.

Soviet Russia Accelerates the Construction of Double Tracks on the Siberian Railway

The Work is Largely Completed Except for the Coastal Provinces

Actively Promoting Colonization of the Far East

Troops are Gathering, Aiming at Self-Defense

(London) The new double tracks of the Siberian Railway, except for a few sections of bridges and tunnels, are now completed. The double tracks of the Amur, Vladivostok, and Dalniy line are also under construction. This was foreshadowed by Chairman Molotov at the People's Committee meeting on February 6th. Once this project is completed, Soviet Russia will still have 1,800 miles of railway that need to be built with double tracks. In the past two years, the policy of the Soviet Russian government has been to strive to enable the Far Eastern Army under General Galen to be self-sufficient. Therefore, it has specially promoted colonization in the Far Eastern territory of Soviet Russia, and granted various special rights, such as exemption from certain taxes and the government buying local products at high prices, to the residents of the area. At the same time, new coal mines are being mined in the Baikal region, and it is said that the production is extremely rich. News from all sides says that there is a thriving scene in the Soviet Russian Far East. The salaries of the army in the Far East have also been increased. Its strength currently totals 150,000 soldiers, and the army is equipped with many artillery pieces and tanks, and there is a gas manufacturing plant. Its headquarters are located in Chita, and it is reported that there are 250 aircraft stationed in Heihe. Moscow has repeatedly stated that this preparation is aimed at self-defense, but from time to time publishes alarming news about Japan's plot to attack Soviet Russia. However, well-informed sources in London say that relations between Japan and Russia have greatly improved in recent weeks. This is evidenced by the conciliatory negotiations between Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota and Soviet Russian Ambassador to Japan Yurenev on the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway. (4th North China Daily News Special Dispatch)

The Doctrine of a Great Air Force Threatens Japan

The World Society says that in recent years, the Soviet Union has actively focused on the progress of the Far East air routes. The Moscow-Irkutsk line has been extended to Vladivostok. Other routes such as the Khabarovsk-Nikolayevsk-Sakhalin route, as well as the route from Marinsk, a stop along that line, to Ayon on Sakhalin, the Verkhoyansk-Kuren route, and the Nikolayevsk-Petropavlovsk route, have all been implemented.

Among the above-mentioned routes, the Khabarovsk-Sakhalin route is the most worthy of our attention. This route began in January 1930, and except for the 4th, 10th, and 11th of each month, it operates every five days on the Khabarovsk-Okha line (taking 8 hours and 45 minutes) and the Khabarovsk-Ayon line (taking 6 hours and 45 minutes). In addition to night flight equipment, the air route has three intermediate airfields and 15 temporary landing fields.

The one that is most threatened by the Soviet Union's doctrine of a great air force is, of course, Japan. If we take Vladivostok as the center point and draw a radius of 1,500 kilometers, which is the range of activity of a modern ordinary bomber, then the entire Korean peninsula, the Kwantung Leased Territory, Manchuria, Hokkaido, the Kuril Islands, Sakhalin, Honshu, Shikoku, Kyushu, Okinawa, and Amami Oshima will all be included in that circle. Even if we take half, 100 kilometers, a large part of Korea and part of the coastal areas of Japan will also be under the threat of enemy aircraft. Recently, the Soviet authorities have been particularly focused on the durability of the range, aiming at the most active attack on Japan, and have been designing and building a TB-2 heavy bomber. The aircraft can carry 16 people, is equipped with an all-domestic M-17 600-horsepower engine, has a top speed of 240 kilometers per hour, and has a range of more than 14 hours. If it advances from Vladivostok to Tokyo, it will only take five hours to reach the skies over Tokyo, and it can comfortably engage in bombing and aerial combat within five hours.

As for fighter planes, the Soviet authorities have recently improved the I-15 (top speed 300 kilometers per hour) fighter plane, equipping it with an all-domestic M-22 700-horsepower engine, increasing the maximum speed to 510 kilometers per hour. It can fly from Osaka to Tokyo in a little over an hour.

The reconnaissance plane is the R-6 type. This is a two-seater aircraft equipped with an all-domestic M-34 800-horsepower engine, with a maximum speed of 240 kilometers per hour and a range of 7 hours. As a medium-range reconnaissance aircraft, its practical value is truly worthy of attention.

Extension of the Non-Aggression Pact Between Russia and Eastern European Countries

Remains in Effect for Ten Years

Only Poland Has Not Signed

(Moscow) Soviet Russia and Estonia, Latvia, and Lithuania have decided to extend the previously signed non-aggression treaty for a new ten-year term. The treaty was jointly signed here on Wednesday by Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov and the ministers of the three countries. The effective period of the treaty has been extended to 1945. Furthermore, the new treaty extending the non-aggression treaty between Soviet Russia and Poland has not yet been signed. (5th Kuomin News Agency)

Contents of the Document

The document has an introduction and two articles of text. The introduction states that the signatory countries signed this document because the signatory countries all wish to find a solid basis for promoting the friendly relations between the aforementioned countries, and are willing to provide new evidence to confirm that their peaceful friendship is appropriate and firm. The introduction also states that the contracting states are inspired by a desire to promote the consolidation of world peace and stability, and the development of peaceful relations between Eastern European countries. The contracting states added that the conclusion of the Mutual Non-Aggression and Peaceful Settlement of Disputes Convention has had commendable effects on their state relations and the resolution of the above-mentioned issues. Article 1 of the text stipulates that the above-mentioned convention and its accompanying documents shall continue to be in effect until December 31, 1945. Article 2 stipulates that this document shall be ratified as soon as possible.

Address by the Russian Foreign Minister

After signing the document, Litvinov delivered a speech saying, "The urgency of our three governments to extend these conventions can express their goodwill and the richness of their accumulated will for peace, and the above two points are further confirmed by the speed with which the Soviet Union's motion was realized in these conventions. This speed is unprecedented in diplomatic history, because only two weeks after the motion was proposed, the document was signed today. Does this not clearly show the long-term growth of mutual trust and understanding between our three countries? We are now extending these conventions for ten years. Ten years is still an initiative in conventions of this nature. However, what we must tell the world is that our proposal is neither temporary in nature nor prompted by accidental economic conditions. In fact, it is a manifestation of our firm policy of peace, so it is not limited by any period of time. One element in this policy is to safeguard the independence of the young countries you represent. The world talks and writes about the war clouds that fill the world every day, and we rarely hear any voices saying that this disaster can be avoided. Governments and politicians all agree that war is inevitable, and what they are considering is only the worldwide rearmament and the arms race. However, the past has clearly shown us that these actions not only cannot avoid war, but can only promote it. However, the document signed today will proclaim to the world that there are now several countries that take the consolidation of peace, at least the consolidation of peace in the region they can influence to some extent, as their international task. These countries will continue to implement their policies to maintain peace in specific regions, and the Soviet Union's policy is to want these countries to join the front line of maintaining peace. All patriotism, nationalism, and racial and ethnic prejudices are irrelevant to the Soviet Union. What the Soviet Union considers its problem is not to conquer others, or expand its influence, nor to expand its own territory. What it cites as its national glory is not militarism and education that does not depreciate the eyes of murderers. The problem and glory of the Soviet Union lies in the realization of its ideal of building a socialist society, because this is where the Soviet Union originated and where the meaning of its own existence lies. If the Soviet Union is not obstructed, it will devote all its strength to this. If someone calls out the list of countries willing to maintain and promote world peace, then they must answer, 'We are here.' Judging from the direct acceptance of our proposal by the countries you represent (this point has been expressed by the document signed today), your countries must also be able to answer in unison with the Soviet Union, 'We are here,' when this list of countries is called out."

Lithuanian Representative's Response

The Lithuanian minister then delivered a reply, deeply believing that the Baltic countries would fully support the great and deeply moving thoughts expressed by the Soviet Foreign Minister, without hesitation. He continued, "The extension of the non-aggression pact is extremely important, because the completion of this move is in a situation where any effort to consolidate world peace has special significance." (4th Havas Dispatch)

The British Government Pays Attention to Diplomacy with Siam

Appointed Crossley as Minister

(London) Sir Crossley, who has been the British Minister to Panama since 1931, has today been appointed British Minister to Siam. Sir Crossley has lived in Siam for many years, serving as consul in various places, so he is familiar with Siamese affairs. (4th Reuters Dispatch)

The King of Siam and His Queen Arrive in Paris and are Welcomed

Today in Turin, Italy, the King of Siam and his Queen visited major automobile factories, hosted by Senator Agli and the local governor. They then went to visit the aircraft factory, where several aviators demonstrated their driving skills. They also went to the Egyptian Museum and the Royal Palace, etc. At 10:00 PM in the evening, the King and Queen, accompanied by their entourage, set off for Paris. (4th Havas Dispatch)

(Paris) After touring Turin today, the King and Queen of Siam officially arrived in Paris by special train. Those who greeted them at the station included French Premier Doumergue and the French Foreign Minister. The Siamese national anthem was played by a military band to welcome them, and many spectators watched outside the station. The French President will host a banquet tomorrow to entertain them. (5th Reuters Dispatch)

Saito Actively Responds to Internal and External Crises

The Army Minister Will Visit Elder Statesmen to State the Military's Views

Konoe Meets with Hirota to Hear His Policy Towards the United States

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Saito has decided to cling to his position regarding cabinet issues, and plans to encourage all cabinet members in tomorrow's cabinet meeting to abandon their previous passive attitude and adopt a more active approach in order to break through international isolation. Regarding measures after withdrawal from the League of Nations takes effect next March and the Second Washington Conference, he should strongly support Hirota's diplomacy. All cabinet members are now also quite united, preparing to deal with all crises with the strength of unity. Regarding the rice control countermeasures and rural relief bills among domestic issues, since he has already decided to cling to his position, he will also actively establish fundamental policies. If there are no sudden changes, Saito said that the cabinet is willing to wait until the crisis of 1936 is over before retiring. (5th China United Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Army Minister Hayashi went to worship at the Kansai Imperial Mausoleum the other day, and plans to return to Tokyo at 10:00 PM tonight. Tomorrow, he will go to Xingxingjin to meet with Saionji to report on the army's budget for this year and the plan to build the Eastern Province. His main purpose is to state the military's attitude towards domestic and foreign policy. According to the army, its policies towards domestic affairs, Manchukuo, and Russia have not changed. Army Minister Hayashi also discussed the military's attitude with General Araki the other day, so this visit to Saionji has aroused much attention from all sectors. (5th China United Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Duke Konoe Fumimaro, speaker of the House of Peers, who is about to go to the United States, met with Foreign Minister Hirota on the afternoon of the 4th to hear Foreign Minister Hirota's opinions on the US issue. After meeting with the Foreign Minister, Konoe told reporters, "I am going to the United States this time in a personal capacity, and it is not necessary for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to send staff to accompany me. However, because I will be meeting with the US President or other dignitaries, I will first listen to Foreign Minister Hirota's entire picture of harmonious diplomacy, especially his policy towards the United States, in order to convey it to the American people. The trip to the United States will last about two months, and I plan to return to the country in early September. There is currently no intention to go to Europe." (5th Japan Alliance Dispatch)

Hirota Puts All His Efforts

To Open Up a Way Out for Japanese-American Diplomacy

China United News Agency Tokyo Correspondence: Since Hirota Hiroki took office as Foreign Minister, his diplomatic understanding has indeed undergone a transformation. Foreign Minister Hirota's approach to handling his diplomacy is the same as that of Uchida, acknowledging the Asian Monroe Doctrine, but his methods are different. Foreign Minister Uchida, disregarding the world's condemnation, strongly implemented the so-called scorched-earth diplomacy with the support of Army Minister Araki's military force. Since he was willing to have the whole country as scorched earth, why bother talking about diplomacy? Foreign Minister Hirota is taking on the position of Foreign Minister to settle this contradiction, that is, to use diplomatic means to achieve the same effect as what would be gained with the strength of a ruined country's military force. Foreign Minister Hirota believes that if Japan wants to carry out its continental policy, the three countries that oppose it most vigorously are Britain, the United States, and Russia, and China is the object of its sacrifice. Britain, because of its domestic unrest, does not dare to lightly engage in war with Japan. Therefore, the only countries that are mortal enemies of Japan are the United States and Russia. Although China wants to resist, its current national strength cannot defeat Japan. If the United States and Russia do not come out to obstruct, then Japan can do whatever it wants in China. This is the basic understanding of Hirota's diplomacy. Under this understanding, Foreign Minister Hirota's only means of breaking the diplomatic deadlock is to first adopt a policy of reconciliation with the United States. If the United States tacitly approves its Eastern policy, the "Manchukuo" issue can be said to be Japan's victory. Under this policy, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs is gathering the elite of its diplomatic circles to attack the United States. There are many important Japanese figures who have been responsible for US diplomacy since the September 18th Incident, including Dr. Nitobe, Duke Tokugawa Iesato (former Speaker of the Upper House), Viscount Ishii Kikujiro (former Foreign Minister), Marquis Matsukata Otogiko (Roosevelt's old classmate), and Duke Konoe Fumimaro (current Speaker of the Upper House, scheduled to go to the United States on May 17). These important figures are working from the sidelines to help Ambassador Saito Hiroshi promote the work of harmonious diplomacy with the United States. Their goals are as follows:

(1) Japan recognizes the permanent neutrality of the Philippines, but the United States must withdraw its land, sea, and air military bases from the island. (2) The United States amends its immigration law to eliminate anti-Japanese clauses. (3) The United States recognizes "Manchukuo" as a fait accompli, and recognizes it at an appropriate time, or no longer reiterates the Stimson Doctrine, while Japan reiterates that "Manchukuo" implements open door and equal opportunity. The Japanese side is also willing to agree with the United States on the security of investment in North China. (4) After the United States agrees to the principles listed on the right, Japan is willing to give up the right to equal armaments. The Japanese Foreign Ministry has proposed this content to the US side. Under this understanding, a ten-year non-aggression treaty can be concluded between Japan and the United States. This is a unilateral demand from the Japanese side. It is certainly not easy for the US side to abandon the Stimson Doctrine given the current domestic situation. Moreover, the content of the non-aggression treaty proposal is more advanced than the content of the Kellogg-Briand Pact of 1928. The US Republican Party has strongly criticized the Japanese side for tearing up this treaty since the September 18th Incident. Although Roosevelt has historical feelings for Japan, it is not easy to reverse the situation. The Japanese Foreign Ministry is also very clear about this point, but it is especially creating an atmosphere and probing US public opinion. Ambassador Saito's report on the various items mentioned on the right after returning to China at the end of May is certainly worthy of our country's attention.

Making Propaganda to the United States

Tokugawa Completes His Mission and Returns Home

(Tokyo) Former Speaker of the House of Peers, Duke Tokugawa Iesato, arrived in Yokohama this afternoon aboard the Japanese ship Tatsuta Maru. Tokugawa told reporters that during his eight months in the United States, he had in-depth discussions with people from all walks of life in the United States on Japanese-American issues, and the atmosphere of friendship between the two countries had become slightly thicker. He denied that a major war would occur between Japan and the United States. Tokugawa broadcast four times in the United States, and gave forty lectures. In his lectures, he strongly denied that Japan had any intention of war against the United States, and opposed the theory of Japanese-American war.

(5th China United Press Dispatch)

Britain Builds Two Largest Airplanes

(London) According to today's news, two large airplanes will appear in Britain. One is the world's largest land airplane, which was ordered by the Royal Airline. It has already been test flown, and its maximum speed is 135 miles per hour, and it usually travels at 108 miles per hour. It can continue to fly for 700 miles, carry 39 passengers, weigh 14.5 tons, and can carry 8,000 pounds of cargo. The other airplane is a sixteen-seat passenger plane that will join the London-Liverpool route on Sunday. It can travel 135 miles per hour, and its operating cost is 1 penny per mile per passenger. (5th Reuters Dispatch)

Britain and America Both Advocate Maintaining Current Naval Ratios

Germany Said to be Participating in Next Year's Naval Conference

Aim is to Seek Revision of the Treaty of Versailles

Hoping to Ensure Maritime Security, Not to Equally Divide Sea Power

(London) According to foreign news reports, the United States seemed to have suggested to Britain that they exchange views before the naval conference in 1935. However, according to British officials, Britain has not received such a suggestion. Since Britain issued a memorandum on disarmament in March 1933, negotiations have continued between London and Washington, so there is no question of proposing an exchange of views. However, the content of the discussions between the two sides concerns the naval tonnage that should be replaced after 1935. So far, no agreement has been reached on this point. It is generally believed that Britain and the United States have no intention of modifying the current naval ratio at the 1935 naval conference, which is evident here. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

(Berlin) Today's newspaper reported that Germany will participate in the naval conference to be held next year. Its purpose is only to seek revision of the Treaty of Versailles in order to obtain greater security at sea, and not to equally divide sea power with the world's major naval powers. The German newspaper also published an official statement denying the claim that Germany plans to embark on a large-scale naval construction program. The report stated that it would take several years for Germany to build a large number of warships, and Germany does not have the financial resources for this. (Reuters dispatch, 4th)

US Battleship Renovation Plan Shelved

To be Discussed After Next Year's Naval Conference

A Glimpse of Concerns About the Situation in the Far East

(Washington) The House Naval Affairs Committee rejected the proposal to renovate the two armored ships, the "California" and the "Tennessee," at a cost of 20 million yuan. Foreign news sources say that this renovation project would take a long time. Once started, the two ships would not be available for use for two or even three years. Therefore, the refusal to start work is a sign of the government's concerns about the Far East issue. Recently, someone inquired about this news to Admiral Standley, Chief of Naval Operations. According to his reply, all obsolete US warships may be destroyed due to future naval agreements, so all renovation plans should be temporarily suspended and considered again after the naval conference next year. The reason why the "California" and "Tennessee" are not being renovated for the time being is nothing more than this. (Havas dispatch, 4th)

Cause of Japanese Torpedo Boat Accident

Lies in Insufficient Righting Moment Against Waves

(Tokyo) Regarding the capsizing of the Japanese torpedo boat "Tomozuru," the inquiry committee headed by Admiral Nomura is conducting a detailed investigation into the cause and other matters. Today, the Ministry of the Navy announced the following: The capsizing of the Tomozuru, after comprehensive investigation, is believed not to be due to the operation of the boat or the watertight integrity of the boat. The main reason is that the righting moment against waves was insufficient. (Dentsu dispatch, 5th)

World Women's Organizations Call for Peace

(Paris) French women have also joined the World Women's Organizations to send a petition to the influential church leaders of various countries. The main purpose of the petition is to promote the unity of church leaders of various countries to promote the movement for world peace. The content of the petition is as follows: [We are the mothers of children, and the children of the world are our children. How can we sit idly by and watch our children slaughter each other without lending a hand? We are women, so whether we believe in God or not, it can be left aside. Our strength can be included in the word "love." Because of love, we boldly disregard the manner of diplomacy. We are so worried about current affairs that we cannot sleep or eat, so we have to petition the spiritual leaders of various religions in the world, such as Gandhi, Besant, and Einstein, and people with ideals and beliefs. We have never forgotten the past efforts of these people (referring to the leaders) to arouse world public opinion, so we cry out to these people by the side of the abyss, saying, "The world has entered a dangerous period. We women can never believe in the authority of international propagators of death, but we are willing to express our faith in the authority of the spirit. Driven by a single thought, we will, in the name of our innocent children, and in the name of mothers' love for their children, earnestly beg the spiritual authorities of the world, because only these people can create a group of sacrifices, continuously and tirelessly, demanding that the governments of various countries lay down their butcher knives." The above petition represents the 800,000 current female teachers from various countries and has been signed by Ms. Bunting, the chairman of the organization. Other organizations listed in the petition include the Education Committee of the World Friendship Alliance of Church Bishops, Gandhi's friends, and the International Women's Association. French Government Issues Austerity Decrees, Civil Servants Rise Up in Resistance

Decide to Launch a General Strike Starting on May 1st

President Voluntarily Reduces Salary as a National Example

(Paris) Today, French Prime Minister Doumergue has signed 15 decrees of the French government to ensure the safety of French finances. The saved government expenses will amount to approximately 2,500,000,000 francs. The contents of the decrees will be announced on Thursday. The main purpose of the government's cost reduction is to reduce official salaries. It is said that in addition to the reduction of official salaries, the French government will also order 68,000 elderly officials to retire. Prime Minister Doumergue's achievement this time is that he implemented it when French finances were in deficit, which can be said to be a decisive move. It is said that previous French prime ministers had also made similar efforts, but the results were complete failures and repeatedly led to the resignation of the cabinet. French officials are very united politically. Previous prime ministers of France have never been able to deal with them successfully. The French national budget for 1934, in addition to a shortfall of 6,000,000,000 francs, still has to repay domestic public debt and other items that are due, amounting to approximately 17,000,000,000 francs. This type of public debt is highly trusted by the French people. (Kokumin dispatch, 4th)

(Paris) After the French government announced the austerity decrees on Wednesday, the employees of the local tax bureau in Metz (a French city) went on strike for half an hour and jointly decided to state to Prime Minister Doumergue that they would take consistent action with other agencies. (Kokumin dispatch, 5th)

(Paris) French civil servants will be greatly affected by the government's salary cuts, so they have risen up in resistance. The Civil Servants Union held a meeting today and decided to notify all members, including employees of public transportation companies, to launch a general strike starting on May 1st until the government withdraws the salary cut plan. It is said that French Prime Minister Doumergue wrote to the President a few days ago, advocating the abolition of concurrent positions and prohibiting the simultaneous receipt of salaries and pensions. Civil servants with lower salaries will have their salaries reduced by 5%, and those with higher salaries will have their salaries reduced by 10%. Gold and Silver

London Gold Price Today (5th) The London gold price is 134 shillings and 8.5 pence, up 5.5 pence from yesterday.

London Silver Today's London silver price for spot is 20 pence, and for futures is 20 pence and 0.0625, both higher than yesterday's closing price by 0.0125. American and Indian buyers entered in the morning, and Chinese buyers bought and then sold. Trading was not active.

New York Silver Today (5th) The silver market opened quietly and steadily, waiting for developments in Washington. It is heard that the Senate will report on Monday or Tuesday on the results of the review of the combined Dawes and Chandler bills. Sentiment is still good. Later, because other markets were hesitant, silver market operators also held back.

Bombay Silver Today (5th) The Bombay silver market closed quietly, with prices up 2 to 4 annas. The spot price is 55 rupees and 2 annas.

Exchange Rates

British and American The London foreign exchange market today (5th) saw sparse trading and was very quiet. The opening exchange rate between British and American currencies was 5.1625 yuan, higher than yesterday's closing exchange rate by 0.0125. There was no change at 11:00 a.m., then it fell slightly. At 2:00 p.m., the price was 5.16125 yuan. Also, one US dollar is equivalent to 3 shillings and 10.5 pence in British currency.

British and French Today's opening exchange rate between London and French currencies was 78.25 francs, lower than yesterday's closing price by three pounds. At 11:00 a.m., it rose three pounds to 78.28 francs. At 1:00 p.m., it fell seven pounds to 78.21 francs. There was no change at 2:00 p.m., but it was four pounds lower than the opening price.

American and British Today (5th) The opening exchange rate between New York and London currencies was 5.1625, higher than the previous day's closing price by 0.0125. The prices at 23:00 were both 5.1550, the lowest at 45:00 was 5.1475, and the price at 6:00 was changed to 5.1500.

American and French Today (5th) The opening exchange rate between New York and French currencies was 6.6.00, higher than the previous day by 0.50.

Cotton and Wheat

Indian Cotton The Bombay cotton market today at 5:30 p.m. saw European exporters buying April-May futures and selling July-August futures. The market closed quietly. The price of July-August Broach cotton was 201.5 rupees, up one rupee from yesterday.

British Cotton The Liverpool cotton market today at 1:00 p.m. had a price of 6.12 for July futures, up six pounds from yesterday.

British Wheat The Liverpool wheat market still had a price of 4 shillings and 5.5 pence for July futures, the same as yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

Australian Official Visits Japan as Prelude to Australia-Japan Negotiations

Aim is to Eliminate Trade War

About to Travel to China

Soejima, an important official of the Australian government, arrived here today and will travel to China, Japan, Hong Kong, Southeast Asia, the Philippines, and Annam for three months. Soejima holds the three positions of Minister of Justice, Foreign Affairs, and Industry in the Australian Cabinet. According to official sources, Soejima's purpose in traveling is to enhance friendly relations between Australia and its neighboring countries and has nothing to do with commerce, but his entourage can provide all necessary information regarding commerce. However, it is generally believed that Soejima's trip has a mission: to negotiate a solution with Japan to avoid the possibility of a trade war between Australia and Japan. Australia had previously proposed increasing import taxes on Japanese goods due to the low value of the Japanese currency. Japan replied that Japan buys more from Australia than it sells to Australia. If Australia raises tariffs, it will be unfavorable to Japan, and Japan will have no choice but to purchase raw materials, such as wool, that it currently purchases from Australia from other markets. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

The United States is About to Implement a Financial Blockade Against Europe

Due to Prolonged Non-Repayment of War Debts by Various Countries

Soviet Russian Debts Will be Handled in the Same Way

(Washington) Today, the Congress completed the formulation of Johnson's proposal. This proposal will deal with the financial markets of the United States, because various countries have promised to repay the debts they previously borrowed from the United States, but they have not been fulfilled. The resolution has been placed in the drawer of President Roosevelt's desk and can be processed immediately upon the President's return from fishing. In the near future, the United States will implement a financial blockade policy against the following countries: Britain, France, Belgium, Poland, Czechoslovakia, Australia, Estonia, Greece, Hungary, Italy, Latvia, Lithuania, Romania, and Yugoslavia. Except for Finland, all European countries are on the list of boycotts. The same steps will be taken to deal with the debts owed by Soviet Russia. Former President Roosevelt had also planned to have the Soviet Russian Import and Export Bank handle the case. Legislative authorities are now studying this issue because the debts were lent during Trotsky's tenure and may be considered a type of war debt. Although Germany's debts are not included in Johnson's proposal, it is generally believed that the debts between the United States and Germany have long been cut off because the interest rates of German banks have been disrupted by foreign public debts. Johnson's proposal is very firm, advocating that the United States will never lend another yuan to European countries. US authorities and US companies, whether individual or investment-oriented, will be prohibited from lending money to countries that have not repaid their debts and will not purchase the public debt tickets of these countries. Last week, the US Treasury Secretary added a correction, saying that there was a claim in Johnson's proposal that a group of New York banks planned to purchase a large number of French public debts and sell them in the United States. The Treasury Secretary has stated that this rumor is untrue. According to Johnson's proposal, it was passed by the Senate in February after reconsideration. (Kokumin dispatch, 4th)

Dike Breaks for Two Hundred Feet in Fukushima Prefecture, Japan

More Than One Hundred Farmers and Fishermen Affected

Hakodate City Reports Another Major Fire

(Tokyo) Since yesterday, the winds and waves have been very high along the coast of Fukushima Prefecture. Today, a seawall in Kitahaba County of the prefecture collapsed for 180 feet, and the surging waves rolled into the fields. More than one hundred farmers and fishermen were affected. The waves are still high at this time, and the residents are in extreme panic. (Hwa Lian dispatch, 5th)

Hakodate, which previously suffered from a huge fire disaster that had just ended, experienced another fire at 10:16 this morning in Kobunemachi. Fortunately, it was daytime, and thanks to the efforts of the fire brigade, it was extinguished at 11:30. More than seventy households were completely destroyed. Among the firefighters, one was seriously injured and one died. The cause of the fire and the losses are currently under investigation. However, the citizens, after the previous major fire, are still like frightened birds, and there was great chaos for a time. (Dentsu dispatch, 5th)

Wang and Chiang Discuss the New Life Movement by Telegram

(Nanchang) Wang Zeng telegraphed Chiang to inquire about the boundaries of the New Life Movement's simplicity, etc. One concern is that it will interfere too much and become a disturbance, and the other is that it will be too ostentatious and turn into hypocrisy. For example, in the previous National Goods Movement in Beijing, shouting "Down with Western suits" caused panic among domestic woolen fabrics and advocating cloth clothing caused silk and satin to have no way out. These must be paid attention to. Chiang replied with two telegrams from Yanjiang, noting that the New Life Movement is to improve old bad habits. It must go from simple to complex, put public interests first and private interests second, extend oneself to others, and go from near and small to far and large. For the time being, the types are limited to rules and cleanliness. Emphasis should be placed on persuasion, not coercion, and guidance should come before supervision. Even if supervision is necessary, it should only apply to civil servants and students. The location should be limited to public places such as machines, schools, roads, docks, theaters, and hotels and should not extend to private bodies and homes. In particular, it is not appropriate for the authorities to take over, losing the interest of the people in participating as a group. The so-called "Four Not's, Six Not's, Ten Commandments, and Eight Precepts" should not be mixed in. (Special dispatch, 5th)

Ministry of Finance Issues Announcement Regarding Methods for Reporting Corruption

(Nanjing) Minister of Finance Kong issued an announcement on the 5th, stating that the agencies under the Ministry of Finance are spread throughout the country. Most officials are diligent, cautious, honest, and self-disciplined, but it cannot be said that there are absolutely no cases of dereliction of duty, corruption, or abuse of power for personal gain. Anyone reporting corruption or laziness must collect evidence, formally submit a complaint, and will be punished according to the law. Those who do not wish to reveal their names will be kept strictly confidential. If the case is significant and there is a concern that the news might leak, evidence can be brought to the ministry for a personal presentation. If the investigation confirms the facts, travel expenses will be reimbursed as appropriate. Those who make false accusations out of malice will be subject to criminal charges and are warned not to attempt it. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 5th)
