The Municipal Council Approves This Year's Budget

The Shanghai Municipal Council's budget for regular and temporary revenue and expenditure for this year, and the financial report for the previous year (1933), were submitted to the Board of Directors meeting by the Finance Committee yesterday and were approved.

According to the report of the Director of Finance to the committee, the actual regular income last year, after making up for the deficit in 1932, was 17,256,357 taels, of which 1,623,490 taels were allocated for education. Regular expenditures, including education expenses, totaled 17,182,001 taels. At the end of the year, there was a surplus of 19,597 taels in ordinary expenses and a surplus of 54,759 taels in education expenses.

In terms of regular income last year, the actual income was approximately 728,000 taels short of the forecast. This was because the initial estimates were inevitably slightly too optimistic, and the number of vacant houses also exceeded expectations. However, at the same time, the various administrative departments were more cautious about the use of funds, and most of the expenses were within the prescribed amount. Therefore, although income decreased, it was still able to break even.

Regarding the interest account, the income exceeded by approximately 25,000 taels, but the proceeds from the sale of the Electricity Department have not been delivered, so this account is unlikely to have any surplus in the future. It is found that the Municipal Council's income in recent years has actually been short of the amount of approximately 2% of the municipal tax. In the past two years, it has been compensated by drawing from the general reserve fund. However, this is only because of the proceeds from the sale of the Electricity Department and cannot be regarded as a regular practice. It is estimated that in recent years, because of this fund, public bonds totaling 37,000,000 taels have been redeemed, and 10,600,000 taels have been allocated to the sinking fund for the 1924-27 public bonds. Moreover, since 1929, construction costs totaling approximately 29,600,000 taels have been paid without resorting to borrowing. Otherwise, the construction expenses and interest on public bonds, calculated at 5.5%, would require a municipal tax of 5% to cover. The Municipal Council's current debt is 19,500,000 taels, while the debt repayment fund has 12,000,000 taels. After offsetting, the actual debt is only 7,500,000 taels.

Regarding the 1934 budget, the estimated total regular income is 24,431,700 yuan, and the total expenditure (including education expenses) is 26,390,060 yuan. The shortfall has been decided to be covered by drawing 2,000,000 yuan from the general reserve fund, with an estimated remaining surplus of 41,640 yuan. Compared with last year, income has increased by 1,280,000 yuan (land tax can be increased by approximately 960,000 yuan, and municipal special tax, license tax, municipal general tax, and wharf tax can all be increased). Expenditure has increased by 1,406,000 yuan, which is largely the natural result of the increase in the business of various administrative departments. However, in the future, the interest account can only have losses and no profits, so the burden on the budget will increase with each year. Therefore, construction plans, except for those that are extremely important, must be tightly controlled.

Regarding the temporary budget for this year, the total amount (excluding temporary education expenses) is 24,710,830 yuan, of which 4,958,570 yuan is the amount of the previous year's deficit. Because there were funds advanced at that time, it was decided not to borrow money to reduce the burden, and this amount was included in this year's budget. As for this year, it is necessary to borrow money or raise 15,500,000 yuan by other means (this level was anticipated in 1930). The specific methods will be submitted to the Board of Directors for deliberation after the annual meeting of ratepayers. As for this year's temporary expenditures, thanks to the practical cooperation of the various directors and the detailed consideration of the various committees, they have been limited to the most urgent and indispensable limit.

The Navigation Administration Bureau Reduces the Burden on Shipping Companies

Since Director Peng took over the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, when technicians of the bureau went out to inspect ships in the past, in addition to shipping companies providing boats and vehicles for transportation, the technicians hired boats and vehicles on their behalf, and the fees paid on their behalf were reimbursed after the shipping companies paid them to the bureau. Approximately 9 yuan for large wheelers and 7 yuan for small wheelers. Director Peng believes that this method is prone to corruption and has decided to abolish it. He has issued a notice to all shipping companies and a letter to the Shipping Association stating that from the first of this month, before the bureau has boat and vehicle equipment, when shipping companies apply for inspection and measurement, they must provide their own boats and vehicles for transportation. Technicians will no longer pay on their behalf, nor will they charge fees from shipping companies, to reduce the burden on merchants. In addition, the bureau will provide the insurance steam valve keys for each ship in the future without additional charges, to alleviate the difficulties of merchants.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Telephones to Request the Cessation of the Collection of License Fees for Small Wheeled Boats in Zhejiang Province

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Communications yesterday, saying: (omitted above) According to a letter from the Shanghai Inland River Shipping Industry Association, the association received a joint letter from members Yuantong and Tongyuan Shipping Bureaus, stating: We respectfully inform you that on December 7th of last year, we received a notice from the Executive Yuan ordering the Zhejiang Provincial Government to stop collecting wheel boat license fees, and we have already instructed our members to comply. However, the Zhejiang Second District Shipping Office and the Pingwang Nanxun Shipping Sub-Office are urgently urging the wheels of the Shenhang Shenhu Line of the Yuantong Bureau to pay fees and obtain licenses, and are also levying donations on the various routes along the way. The wheels of the Shengjia Jiahu Line of the Tongyuan Bureau are being urged by telephone to collect fees, as urgently as a fire. The Executive Yuan has already ordered Zhejiang Province to stop collecting wheel boat license fees, so why are they not complying? The office replied that the suspension of wheel boat license fees refers to ships that are numbered by the Marine Fisheries Administration Bureau. Whether this statement is true or whether the office is disobeying orders and misinterpreting them is unknown. We, as ignorant people, feel at a loss. Therefore, we telegram Your Association to examine the situation and forward it to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Communications, begging for a clear explanation as to whether the Zhejiang license fees for our wheel boat industry are not included in the suspension of collection. Please also consult the Zhejiang Provincial Government and Qian, the director of the Second District Shipping Office, that before the Executive Yuan issues an interpretation, they must not force donations or fees from the wheels of the Yuantong and Tongyuan Bureaus, for the sake of public well-being. According to this, after investigating, the Executive Yuan had already notified the Zhejiang Provincial Government in February of this year to stop collecting wheel boat license fees. Now, the Zhejiang Second District Shipping Office is still forcing the collection, which is not only a violation of the glorious order, but also a disturbance to merchants and harm to the people. Furthermore, the office replied that the suspension of wheel boat license fees refers to ships that are numbered by the Marine Fisheries Administration Bureau. This argument has no legal basis. At a time when the shipping industry is declining, it is absolutely inappropriate to engage in exploitation and increase the burden on the shipping industry. According to the situation in the letter, we specially telegram Your Association to beg you to forward it to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Communications, and quickly order the Zhejiang Provincial Government to instruct the Zhejiang Second District Shipping Office to stop collecting fees, in order to alleviate the people's difficulties and maintain the shipping industry, which is for the benefit of the public. etc. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce salutes. After investigating, the original text of the Executive Yuan's No. 3066 instruction of last year states: After investigation, the Maritime Law stipulates that ships with a total tonnage of 26 tons and a capacity of more than 200 dan have been registered by the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications in accordance with the law, and tonnage inspection certificates and ship nationality certificates have been issued. Local government offices in various provinces should no longer order these ships to apply for licenses and collect fees, resulting in a situation of double taxation. The provincial government is ordered to comply. The wheel boats of the various member bureaus of the association, which sail on the inland rivers of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, are all ships of more than 20 tons, and have all been registered with your ministry and the Ministry of Communications in accordance with the law, and have obtained inspection tonnage nationality certificates. The verification complies with the regulations of the Executive Yuan that provinces should not double-collect license fees. The said Executive Yuan order was issued to Zhejiang Province last year, and newspapers have already published it. The Zhejiang Second District Shipping Office has neither complied with the order to stop collecting fees, and has misinterpreted the Executive Yuan order. Its situation is particularly harmful to merchants and violates the law. It is reasonable to telegraph Your Yuan Ministry to examine and verify, and to order the Zhejiang Provincial Government to instruct them to stop collecting fees, in order to comply with the Yuan order, which is for the benefit of the public. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce salutes.

The Case of the Arrest of Union Cadres at the Wusong Machinery Factory

Union Branches from Two Railway Lines Telegraph the Party Headquarters, Urgently Requesting Rescue Efforts

Party Headquarters Expresses Their Position, Responding to the Railway Bureau with a Demand for Cautious Handling

The Special Party Headquarters of the Two Railway Lines issued a statement saying that all workers at the Wusong Machinery Factory of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways had, in December of last year, reported Ying Heng, the chief of the General Affairs Department and concurrently chief of the Materials Department of the two railway lines, for defaming the Party Headquarters, undermining the labor movement, abusing his authority, and engaging in corruption. They telegraphed the Party Headquarters and the unions of the two lines, requesting them to send personnel to investigate, handle the matter impartially, and petition the Central Government and the Ministry of Railways to dismiss and punish Mo Heng. At that time, the Fujian Incident was occurring, and the Party Headquarters and unions of the two lines, in order to avoid escalating the situation, sent personnel to earnestly persuade and explain to the workers of the entire factory. At the same time, they petitioned the Central Government to order the Ministry of Railways to handle the matter impartially, and work was resumed, restoring the original situation. Later, the Ministry of Railways sent personnel to investigate, and as a result, determined that Mo Heng, the chief of the General Affairs Department and concurrently chief of the Materials Department, had spoken incautiously, causing a misunderstanding and leading to the incident. The Ministry of Railways reprimanded Mo Heng, and he was given a warning. All problems were also resolved.

The Course of Events Leading to the Arrest of All Cadres

On the morning of March 30th of this year, at approximately 10:00 AM, Huang Boqiao, the director of the two railway lines, ostensibly convened a meeting with all the cadres of the branch office of the factory's union for discussions. Simultaneously, he secretly colluded with the police department of the two railway lines and the Municipal Public Security Bureau to entice and arrest ten cadres from the factory's union branch office: Cao Wenkui, Lin Jinlin, Li Kuikui, Tang Genfa, Xu Shanqing, Shi Genyuan, Han Weiyu, Zhou Weixian, Chen Shusheng, He Laixing, and others. They were put on a car and sent to the headquarters.

The Union Telegrams the Party Headquarters for Rescue

After the case occurred, the unions of the two railway lines immediately convened an urgent meeting. It was resolved to send personnel to thoroughly investigate the case and to appoint Director Min Luoheng to inquire with the Garrison Headquarters about the truth of the matter in order to reasonably respond to the Railway Bureau. They also telegraphed the Party Headquarters of the two railway lines, explaining the truth and seeking ways to rescue them. The original telegram is excerpted below (omitting the titles): Your esteemed consideration, upon investigating, on the day of the 30th of March, Huang Boqiao, the director of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau, convened all the cadres of the Wusong Machinery Factory branch office of the two railway lines' union in the conference room of the Shanghai North Station Transportation Office under the pretext of holding discussions. Except for Tang Dafa and Zhu Derong, who were absent due to illness, the remaining eighteen people, Xu Shanqing, Lin Jinlin, Li Kuiyuan, Cao Wenkui, Tang Genfa, Chen Shusheng, Zhou Weixian, Shi Zhenyuan, He Laixing, Han Weiyu, and others, were suddenly arrested by railway police during the discussions and escorted to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters. All the employees of the railway were shocked upon hearing the news, but the reason for the arrest was unknown for a time. It was not until April 1st that the Shanghai newspapers contained detailed reports, stating that the cadres were arrested because the Wusong workers had filed a complaint against Mo Heng, the chief of the General Affairs Department and concurrently chief of the Materials Department of the Railway Bureau, which had resulted in a work stoppage in December of last year. Upon investigation, the work stoppage on that day was due to the workers' accusations against Mo Heng for insulting the Party and the country, undermining the labor movement, abusing his authority, and engaging in corruption. They listed the facts and earnestly requested the Railway Bureau to dismiss him from his post and investigate him, and sent representatives to the Railway Bureau to present their views. However, the Railway Bureau, considering the case to be related to the Railway Bureau's scandalous affairs, tried its best to whitewash it. The workers were even more indignant to see the Railway Bureau glossing over the situation in this way, and they all believed that in order to uphold Party affairs and the labor movement and to rectify official corruption, it was necessary to ask Chief Mo to personally come to the Songhu office to explain. They had already obtained Mo's agreement, who promised to go immediately, but day after day, he never set foot in the Song factory and did not notify the workers. Waiting for Mo's explanation led to the work stoppage. If it was a case of absenteeism, it should have been handled through legal procedures. Moreover, it was during the Fujian Incident, so how could they willingly step into the trap of the law? Therefore, Mo Heng was fully responsible for the work stoppage on that day. The union, considering the situation to be serious, sent personnel to guide the workers in various ways. Since the Railway Bureau refused to accept the case, the workers had no choice but to go to Beijing to petition the Central Government and the Ministry of Railways in order to clarify the Railway administration. Subsequently, the Ministry of Railways sent personnel to Shanghai to thoroughly investigate, but the Railway Bureau again used deceptive tactics to deceive the special commissioner, covering up the facts and siding with Mo Heng. Fortunately, your esteemed association, under the leadership of the Central Government, guided the union and announced that they should work with peace of mind and file another petition for resolution. The workers, deeply understanding the righteousness during the Fujian Incident, gradually eased the situation. However, three months have passed since then, and the workers are still working as usual without any accidents. Since the Ministry had approved the investigation and handling, they should wait patiently for the resolution. Therefore, they abided by national laws and did not dare to make unreasonable demands. Unexpectedly, the Ministry of Railways has delayed the decision for a long time, and the Railway Bureau has recently appointed Qiu Weiying, Li Xuanyu, Wang Shufang, and others to work at the Wusong Machinery Factory. The workers believe that the Railway Bureau has always used the slogan of saving Railway funds, but now it has suddenly added a large number of personnel to serve in the factory, increasing public funds by more than a thousand yuan per month, which is a waste of Railway funds. Why are all the workers' previous requests always rejected? This shows that the Railway Bureau's rectification of Railway administration and saving of Railway funds are just self-deceptive slogans. On March 21st, the Railway Bureau persuaded Chen Chengshi, the chief of the Car Affairs Section of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the current executive member of the Party Headquarters of the two railway lines, to accompany Qiu and Wang to the factory to explain to the workers. However, a portion of the workers began to make noise before he finished speaking, and even threw debris, causing Chen to be injured and bleed on his forehead. On the 28th, the Railway Bureau issued an order to the union, stating that the workers' actions were lawless and undisciplined. If they were not corrected, what would become of the situation? It asked whether these rioters belonged to the Wusong Machinery Factory branch of the union, who was the instigator, and who was the accomplice. It ordered the union to investigate and report the details within three days of receiving the document for verification and handling. The union also believed that the actions of a few workers were rash and inappropriate. It was immediately decided to convene a meeting of the cadres of the branch office on the afternoon of March 30th to review the situation at the factory at the time of the incident. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the same day at 11:00 AM, the cadres were arrested at the North Station. At the same time, the Railway Bureau issued Order No. 129 of the General Department, stating that the workers of the Wusong Machinery Factory and the Materials Factory had previously accused Mo Heng, the chief of the General Affairs Department and concurrently chief of the Materials Department, and simultaneously implemented a work stoppage. Now, the Ministry of Railways has issued Order No. 8736, instructing the following: (1) The original accusations have been investigated and found to be without evidence and should be dismissed. (2) Chief Mo's incautious remarks caused a misunderstanding and should be given a warning. (3) The workers of the factory did not resolve the matter according to the law and instead engaged in a work stoppage to coerce, and Cao Wenkui has not yet complied with the transfer to Ningbo, which is inappropriate and should be handled according to the law. The Bureau will comply with these instructions. Upon investigation, the cadres of the Wusong Machinery Factory branch of the union not only did not stop the previous work stoppage, but also violated the law by directly publishing articles to the outside world, and the directors and supervisors of the union did not correct them, which is inappropriate. At that time, the Central Government was suppressing the Fujian rebellion, and Shanghai was a key rear area. The Railway's military transport was also very tight. However, the two factories suddenly experienced a work stoppage, almost delaying the overall situation, which is extremely regrettable. The Railway has always been known as a model Railway, but now it has such a disreputable behavior, which is also very regrettable. The union's handling was inappropriate and should be reprimanded. The illegal actions of the Wusong Machinery Factory branch of the union should be discussed and dealt with by the union, and they should be warned not to have such out-of-bounds actions in the future, which is of utmost importance. It can be seen that the Railway Bureau should handle the case in accordance with the Ministry's orders, and the occurrence of this case was due to Mo Heng's defamation of the Party Headquarters, undermining of the labor movement, abuse of authority, and engagement in corruption. Mo Heng should bear full responsibility. Now, Mo Heng, with his guilty body, has escaped legal punishment, while the workers who filed the complaint according to the law have been arrested. There is nothing more bizarre than this. Moreover, the document mentions that the union should discuss and deal with the matter, but without waiting for the union's discussion and decision, it used emergency measures to entice and arrest all the cadres, which is even more absurd. The union sent personnel to Wusong to investigate the reason for the cadres' arrest. Unexpectedly, the Railway Bureau's notice had already been posted in the factory, stating that in December of last year, the workers of the Wusong Machinery Factory and the Wusong Materials Factory went on strike for a week under the pretext of various reasons, causing the Railway to lose huge sums of money. They also incited other workers to respond. At that time, the Central Government was suppressing the Fujian rebellion, and Shanghai was under martial law. The military transport of the two lines was very important. It was reported that reactionary elements were manipulating the situation, attempting to disrupt the overall situation. Now, the Ministry has ordered that this work stoppage should be handled according to the law. In addition to removing the employees who instigated the labor unrest in accordance with Article 30 of the Railway Employee Service Regulations, they should be transferred to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for investigation and punishment in accordance with the order of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Military Affairs Commission. It also stated that the Railway Bureau had reported to the Ministry of Railways, which was then ordered by the Ministry of Railways via telegram, which had been forwarded to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Military Affairs Commission for approval, outlining two points: (1) Cao Wenkui should be punished by the Songhu Garrison Headquarters to the fullest extent of the law. (2) If the Wusong Machinery Factory attempts to strike again, the Songhu Garrison Headquarters will immediately send the Shanghai Municipal Security Team to severely suppress it. The Bureau has complied with the order and executed it on March 30th. From the above observations, it is clear that the Railway Bureau has a deep-seated hatred and resentment towards the Wusong workers for reporting the Mo Heng case and is eager to seize an opportunity to vent its personal anger. Considering the Railway Bureau's extreme hatred and resentment towards Cao Wenkui and the other cadres of the Wusong Machinery Factory branch, the focus is on the Railway Bureau's mistaken belief that Cao Wenkui and others were the instigators of the report against Mo Heng. Therefore, it did not hesitate to fabricate charges against Cao and others and imprison them, which is truly painful to say. Because the cadres had difficulty restraining the workers during the work stoppage, they used the pretext of affecting the military transport of the Fujian rebellion, deliberately exaggerating the situation in order to shift the blame to the workers, fabricating facts. The Railway Bureau's deception of superiors and subordinates, sudden use of emergency measures, and illegal enticement and arrest of all cadres, where are Party discipline and national law? Upon investigation, the Ministry of Railways has determined that Mo Heng's incautious remarks caused a misunderstanding and has clearly ordered him to be warned. It is clear that Mo Heng should bear full responsibility for the cause of the work stoppage. Now, the Railway Bureau has completely shifted the blame to all the cadres and arrested them all, reversing right and wrong and greatly affecting the Party's and the people's future in the labor movement. We earnestly request your esteemed association to forward this to the Central Government and to telegraph Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to quickly order the Songhu Garrison Headquarters to investigate the truth, allow the release of all the innocent arrested cadres, so as to benefit the labor movement and reassure the public. The telegram ends with extreme anxiety and urgent waiting for orders, the Railway Union directly under the Ministry of Railways, Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, respectfully.

Hu Xiyuan's Opinion on the Interpretation of Trademarks by the Judicial Court

After Hu Xiyuan of the Electric Appliance Industry expressed his opinion on the second paragraph of Article 1 of the Trademark Law, which was interpreted by the Judicial Court, it aroused great attention from the industrial sector. The various industrial groups expressed their opinions one after another in order to remedy the situation. The industrial colleagues took Hu's written opinion as more detailed, so they asked the China Federation of Industrial Associations and Hu himself to review the original text, and in order to gather wisdom and benefit everyone's research, the original book is published as follows, for reference (略略略) Regarding the explanation of the second paragraph of Article 1 of the Trademark Law, only the shape of the word is discussed, and the sound is not asked. The industrial sector is not only anxious because of the personal interests of the industrial sector, but also has some inconsistencies in the legal and sentimental affairs. Now, let me say it separately, (1) The sixth item of Article 2 of the Trademark Law [the same or similar to the trademark used by others in the world for the same commodity] shall not be presented for registration as a trademark, and the [similar] two words have a wide range and have no express provisions for formal similarity, then it clearly includes the similarity of sound, which is among them, and the dispute of trademarks will necessarily arise from the commodity known in the world. If the name of the commodity has not been announced, except for special circumstances, there will be no trademark dispute, and even the strong people will use the same trademark, I am afraid that they will also frown and will not follow, and the article gives strong protection to the famous goods, and now if only the shape of the word is discussed, regardless of the sound, the original intention of the article will be completely destroyed.

Health Bureau Announces Shooting of Horses with Glanders

A Total of Twenty-Eight

The Daily News reports that yesterday, the Health Bureau announced that glanders in horses is extremely harmful, not only spreading among the herd but also posing a threat to humans. Not only is their flesh poisonous and highly dangerous, but their urine, saliva, and milk can also transmit the disease. Therefore, farmers who raise horses, grooms who tend horses, and soldiers in the army are often tragically killed by this disease. This is a matter of great concern for public health. Thus, Director Li ordered the slaughter of the horses. The horses had to be sent to the Health Laboratory for blood tests. The first test results revealed that twenty-eight horses were infected with glanders. Director Li, considering the importance of public health and national defense, did not hesitate to sacrifice the harmful horses. He requested the City Government to approve the destruction of all the infected horses by shooting and burning. To alleviate the hardship of the owners, the City Government will provide appropriate subsidies. Mayor Wu approved the request, and Section Chief Wang of the Second Division consulted with the Public Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) to assist in the execution of the twenty-eight diseased horses. The SMC Public Health Department, recognizing the importance of public health, assisted in shooting and burning the diseased horses one by one the day before yesterday, eliminating them completely. This constitutes a new record in public health administration. In the future, the Health Laboratory will continue to actively inspect horses, and a request has been submitted to the National Health Administration to inform domestic industrial operators that many imitate but lack creativity. If one industry shows even a slight profit, everyone flocks to it, resulting in mutual destruction. The few who possess extraordinary ability and are not crushed and overturned simultaneously rely on the protection of trademark law. If we only consider the form and disregard the sound, the protection afforded by trademarks loses most of its effectiveness. Moreover, if a new product in an industry seeks a trademark that sounds the same as an established brand, their intentions are obvious. The reason they did not attempt this before was because they knew that the application of Article 1, Section 2 of the Trademark Law would not be favorable under previous interpretations. Now that the new interpretation facilitates considering form without regard to sound, the trend of allusive imitation will grow daily. This is the fifth point. (6) Considering the current environment, the market is flooded with inferior goods. Unscrupulous merchants, driven by greed, are racking their brains to counterfeit domestic goods. They are somewhat deterred by the protection of trademark law, so they must hide their intentions and dare not do so openly. If the interpretation of the Trademark Law disregards sound, they will blatantly engage in counterfeiting. If so, there will be no hope for domestic goods. This is the sixth point. In conclusion, if the interpretation of Article 1, Section 2 of the Trademark Law is not corrected, not only will trademark disputes never cease, but the future of the industrial sector will also become increasingly troubled and gradually approach extinction. I have not studied law, but what I have said above is not an exaggeration. Feeling a sense of danger, I dare not remain silent. Therefore, I have further elaborated on what was not fully covered in my previous letter, focusing on what will inevitably occur in reality. (End of excerpt)

Shanghai Market Dominated by Superior Chinese Cement

Daily News Claims Chinese Goods Exclusively Occupy the Market

Japanese Goods Trapped in a Desperate Situation

According to the Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun yesterday, since last year, the situation of cement in this port has been such that Chinese goods were originally priced at five dollars and seventy or eighty cents per barrel, while Japanese goods were cheaper, selling for only four dollars and forty or fifty cents. However, the Chinese side, using anti-Japanese sentiment, worked hard to maintain the market price and compete with Japanese goods. Although Japan's Onoda and Asano jointly stood on the front lines of competition, the Chinese side suddenly lowered prices, reducing the price per barrel to five dollars and twenty cents, with a difference of only thirty or forty cents compared to Japanese goods. In addition, the National Government recently added import duties, approximately one dollar and sixty cents per dan (a unit of weight). As a result, Japanese goods had to increase their market price. Because Japanese goods became more expensive, Chinese merchants hardly considered them at all. Currently, Japanese goods are in a desperate situation. On the other hand, Chinese goods have exclusively occupied the local market. Even imports from Soviet Russia have suffered a similar blow due to increased taxes, and are experiencing the same difficulties as Japanese goods.

Telephone Company Disconnecting Lines Without Reason Should Compensate for Losses

Chinese Ratepayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council Yesterday

Strictly Managing the Powers of Franchise Businesses

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you regarding a complaint from the Zhonghua Box Factory stating that at 7:30 AM on the 29th of this month, the taxpayer's telephone line, number 53373, was disconnected by the Shanghai Telephone Company without reason, making it unusable. The factory immediately borrowed telephone number 53349 to inquire with the Business Department of the Shanghai Telephone Company, and was told that the 53373 telephone line had indeed been cut off. The taxpayer's telephone bill for this quarter was paid in full on March 17th, as evidenced by the receipt. However, the Telephone Company, without careful investigation, abruptly stopped the telephone service, deliberately neglecting its duties, for which it should be held responsible. We then borrowed telephone 53349 and directed our Huaji Road office to use telephone 52922 to inquire with the Business Department of the Telephone Company, but the staff replied that the telephone bill had not been paid or that the matter was not their concern. We also inquired with extension 01 and the accounting department, but received the same responses. Until there was a concrete response, for such a large franchised business organization, the internal disorder is inexplicable, disregarding the rights of its users and acting arbitrarily. We then negotiated several more times, and finally received an inquiry from 11044, which referred us to 15960. Upon calling 15960, we only heard a vague statement that they were aware of the matter, without explaining the reason for the disconnection. After several more reminders, the line was finally reconnected at 1:30 PM. The total time of unjustified disconnection was six hours, from 7:30 AM to 1:30 PM. The losses suffered by our factory in terms of business and reputation were significant and substantial. During this disconnection, our factory's customers assumed that our factory's financial situation was dire, unable to even pay the telephone bill, resulting in the Telephone Company abruptly taking action, stopping the telephone service, causing a major misunderstanding and leading to much discussion and speculation, all of which was caused by the Telephone Company. Therefore, the company cannot evade responsibility for this unjustified disconnection. Our factory, being a taxpayer, has reported the facts to your Association, and requests that you forward this letter to the Municipal Council, which is responsible for managing and supervising franchised businesses, and instruct the Telephone Company to compensate our factory for the losses suffered in terms of business and reputation, as a warning for the future. We hope that your Council will promptly exercise its authority to supervise and manage franchised businesses and order them to compensate the victims for their losses, demonstrating the intention to safeguard public utilities." Addressed to the General Manager of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council.

Xin Jiangtian Encountered Fog and Almost Ran Aground

Dangerous Situation, Narrow Escape

Crew and Passengers Rejoice in Their Survival

Last Saturday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xin Jiangtian departed from Shanghai. The ship was carrying as many as 1,700 to 1,800 passengers. To prevent pirates, the exterior iron gates were locked after the ship set sail. That night, the fog was thick and difficult to navigate. Because it was a scheduled run, the ship could not delay its departure, so it continued to sail. At 2:43 AM, the ship passed the Daxiaoji Islands. The sea was not visible, so it anchored to wait for the fog to clear before continuing, showing caution. In that sea area, there is a lighthouse called Valaon, which is located in an area full of hidden reefs, making it the most difficult area to navigate. A lighthouse was built there to guide the ships. Opposite the lighthouse is an area of clustered reefs. After the Xin Jiangtian anchored, it could not find the lighthouse. It was suspected that it had not yet arrived, and was still searching. At this time, Chief Navigator He Hongyao was on duty and ordered to steer to the right, intending to follow the Ningxing route. In fact, the Xin Jiangtian was anchored next to the lighthouse. The lighthouse light was obscured by the fog. Chief Navigator He Hongyao ordered to steer to the right, believing that the Ningxing route was viable for this ship as well. After only one minute of sailing, the captain urgently ordered to stop and wait to identify the direction before proceeding. At 2:48 AM, the fog cleared slightly. The crew on deck discovered a large black mountain ahead of the ship and rushed to report to the captain to quickly reverse the engines, as they were already in the reef zone. Fortunately, the captain had ordered to stop, because in just two more minutes, the entire ship would have run aground and been smashed to pieces. The danger was extremely close. They quickly reversed the engines and returned to the original anchorage near the lighthouse to wait for the fog to clear before proceeding. At that time, all the crew members were frightened and lost color, all claiming it was a great stroke of luck. If the captain had not stopped the ship, the Xin Jiangtian would have caused an unprecedented tragedy. Moreover, the passenger cabins were mostly locked, and if an accident had occurred, none of the passengers would have survived. It was truly a stroke of luck. After the ship returned to Shanghai, the crew members said that this time they had survived a disaster, and their lives were like being reborn. If the captain had not ordered to stop, the consequences would have been unspeakable. When the crew members arrived in Shanghai and spoke to others, they all expressed their good fortune.

The Changde Bao immediately went to investigate and report to the Sixth District for investigation.

The Horrific Scene of the Murder: After receiving the report, District Chief Tan sent Inspector Cheng, along with Police Chief Hu, to investigate. They found that the unidentified male corpse was approximately 30 years old, wearing a black cotton-padded jacket, blue cloth trousers, gray cotton socks, and blue imitation serge shoes. He was bald and had no hat, appearing to be a worker. Beside him was a blank diary, a cigarette case containing a pawn ticket. The lower half of his body was inserted into the mud at the bottom of the canal, while the upper half floated on the surface. The temples, forehead, tip of the nose, side of the mouth, and left cheek had sustained five or six knife wounds. There was a severe wound on the back of the head and another on the front of the neck, where the throat bone had been severed, with blood and flesh blurred, a truly tragic sight. It appeared that he had been murdered elsewhere and his body dumped here.

Request for Autopsy: District Chief Tan, considering that the case involved assassination, immediately ordered the detective team and the police officers under his command to strictly arrest the murderer for punishment. At the same time, he ordered Wang Songsheng, the local head of the 12th tu (a unit of households), to report to the local court for an autopsy. At 2:00 PM, Prosecutor Wu from the court arrived at the scene and determined that the unidentified male corpse had indeed been murdered. He ordered the local head to prepare a coffin for burial and ordered an investigation into the identity of the deceased's family and the arrest of the murderer for further investigation.

Ships Carrying Dangerous Goods for Import Must Notify the Harbor Master in Advance

Gu Lien, Harbor Master of the Jianghai Customs, issued Bulletin No. 11 yesterday, stating: "Hereafter, for any ships carrying dangerous goods, whether for import to Shanghai, transshipment, or passing through Shanghai, the Harbor Master's Office must be notified at least forty-eight hours before the ship arrives in Shanghai. If there is any doubt as to whether the goods are dangerous, the matter should also be reported to this office for determination. All ship managers and owners are hereby informed. Issued by Harbor Master Gu Lien."

Municipal Council Reviews Applications for Hotel and Restaurant Licenses

The Public Safety Committee of the Municipal Council held a special meeting on March 22 to review applications for hotel and restaurant licenses. Major Darby of the Salvation Army, and Messrs. Milligan, Fitch, Todd, Thomas, and one representative of a Japanese women's group attended the meeting. Major Darby stated that a large portion of the foreign community, especially the poor, suffered greatly from alcohol. Chinese wine and vodka were often sold in the alleys, and the poor, attracted by the low prices, would indulge in drinking, causing damage to their spirits and bodies, making it difficult to find work, and sometimes getting drunk and having their clothes stolen. Therefore, the issuance of liquor licenses should be strictly controlled, and the practice of issuing temporary licenses should be abolished. Mr. Fitch also said that there were already too many taverns, and the hours for selling alcohol should be further restricted. After discussion, the following decisions were made: (A) Applications for hotel licenses: 1. 287 Yunnan Road, 2. 164 Jing'an Temple Road, 3. 218 and 238 Yuyuan Road, 4. 873 North Sichuan Road, 5. 422 Tiantong Road. Except for the fourth one, which is not allowed to set up a public bar, all are approved. (B) Applications for hotel licenses: 6. 3A Xinkang Road, 7. 440 Sichuan Road, 8. 500 Tibet Road, 9. 216 Jing'an Temple Road, 10. 1269 Jing'an Temple Road, 11. 6 Dahua Road, 12. 139 Broadway Road, 13. 863 North Sichuan Road, 14. 93 Seward Road. All are approved, but the sixth one must be handled according to the instructions of the Works Department. Regarding applications for hotel licenses in movie theaters, as there were no violations, it was deemed unnecessary to change or add restrictions. Regarding the general restriction of alcohol sales hours, it was deemed to be closely related to the current policy, and no suggestions were made. (C)

Applications for restaurants (serving alcohol with meals) licenses: 15. 565 Nanjing Road, 16. 795 Jing'an Temple Road, 17. 870 Jing'an Temple Road, 18. 918 North Sichuan Road, 19. 368 Tiantong Road, 20. 10 Wiesen Lane, 21. 12 and 24 Lane 429 Wusong Road, 22. 662 Broadway Road, 23. 1-3 Yuanchang Road, 24. 6-8 Yuanchang Road. Except for numbers 22 and 23, which were rejected based on the opinions of the Police Department, the rest were approved. (D) Applications for beer and other ale licenses: 25. 104 Central Building, 26. Opposite 729 Fuxu Road, 27. 226-230 Jing'an Temple Road, 28. 1178 Jing'an Temple Road, 29. 1179 Jing'an Temple Road, 30. 224-226 Baker Road, 31. 27 Lane 1000 Gordon Road, 32. 4 Lane 455 Haifang Road, 33. 6 Peng Road, 34. 7 Lane 15A Peng Road, 35. 47 Peng Road, 36. 8 Lane 72 Peng Road, 37. 105 Peng Road, 38. 2258-9 Peng Road, 39. 101 Zhapu Road, 40. 336-338 Zhapu Road, 41. 358 Zhapu Road, 42. 306-308 Haining Road, 43. 125 Nanxun Road, 44. 404 North Suzhou Road. The twenty-sixth one will be approved after complying with the methods specified by the Health Department. The thirty-seventh one was rejected because the applicant had moved out of the address. The forty-third one was rejected based on the reasons given by the Police Department. The rest were approved. Furthermore, applications for renewal from those who have already obtained licenses for categories A, B, C, and D were also approved. The Committee's proposal was submitted to the Board of Directors and has been approved for implementation.

Shanghai Silk Industry Bank Held Its Third Annual General Meeting Yesterday

Ratified the Capital Increase Plan and Revised Articles of Association

Elected Directors and Supervisors

The Shanghai Silk Industry Bank, located at 460 Hankou Road, has been established for three years. Yesterday at 1:00 PM, the bank held its third annual general meeting at the Banking Association at 4 Hong Kong Road. In addition to all the directors, supervisors, and deputy managers, more than 300 shareholders attended, including Qian Xinzhi, Wang Shoushan, Tao Changhai, Xu Xinliu, Kui Yanfang, and Wu Yunchu. The meeting was declared open at 1:00 PM. After the usual formalities, Chairman Wang Yansong gave a report on the business situation, stating that the bank's development in terms of organization and business over the past year could be summarized in four points: (1) Increasing Capital: The bank's original capital was 600,000 yuan. Last year, as business gradually developed and credit grew, it was decided at the previous shareholders' meeting to increase the capital by 400,000 yuan. Later, due to enthusiastic investment from all parties, the amount exceeded the original amount. At the twenty-third board meeting, it was decided to revise the amount to 600,000 yuan, and the full amount has now been raised. (2) Establishing Branch Offices in the City: Recognizing the wealth of the residents and the prosperity of the shops in the French Concession, the bank established a branch in Baixianqiao to facilitate customer transactions. This was the first branch established by the bank. Following this, the bank prepared to establish a branch in Nanshi, leasing and renovating the old premises of the Social Affairs Bureau at Xiaonanmen, which opened on March 21st of this year. It is expected that the bank's relationship with the people of Shanghai South and Shanghai West will grow, and the bank will be able to reap the benefits. (3) Joining the Banking Association: Recognizing the bank's increasingly solid position and the progress of its business, the bank believed that it should have appropriate connections with its peers. In January of this year, it joined the Shanghai Banking Association as a member bank. (4) Establishing Voucher Contract: In order to expand its business, the bank has successively entered into contracts with banks such as the Central Trust and Commerce Bank to issue and redeem vouchers, totaling 2.5 million yuan. Other major businesses, such as deposits, loans, receipts, and payments, are growing daily. In addition, businesses such as the real estate department, safekeeping department, and warehouse department are also thriving. Furthermore, the bank has established a general affairs department in the head office to improve efficiency. The bank plans to establish a branch in Hangzhou, which is currently being prepared and is scheduled to open this month. In general, the bank has been striving to promote business under the principle of "seeking progress in stability," and is grateful for the guidance and support of the shareholders. Therefore, the bank's future is unlimited. Next, Supervisor Xu Jilong reported on the accounts. The meeting then passed two proposals submitted by the board of directors: (1) To approve the distribution of last year's profits according to the articles of association. The proposal was approved. (2) To approve the report on the surplus from the capital increase. The proposal was approved. Next, a representative of the board of directors reported on the progress of soliciting new shares. Then, the supervisor gave an investigation report on the capital increase. Next, the board of directors proposed to amend the bank's articles of association, including amendments to Articles 8, 36, and 52, as well as Articles 1, 3, and 5 of the Savings Department's original articles. Finally, the meeting elected directors and supervisors, including Wang Yansong, Yu Zuoting, Wang Boyuan, Zhang Tanru, Pei Yunqing, Feng Zhongqing, Chen Xiaodie, Sun Hegao, Chen Ziming, Shen Qinzai, Chen Songyuan, Shou Yicheng, and Wang Boying as directors, and Xu Jilong, Cheng Yongliu, Ge Shuqian, and Lu Zhengbing as supervisors. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Smashing a Secret Destruction Bureau

Detaining a Substitute and Summoning Witnesses for Verification

Since the Ministry of Finance implemented the abolition of taels and the conversion to the yuan, the private destruction of national currency for recasting into silver ingots has been strictly prohibited, and orders have been issued to all provinces, cities, and counties for compliance. Last night at 8:30 PM, the First Precinct of the Second District of the city, acting on a tip, reported that Wu Yu Ji Sand Shop at No. 45 Fuyou Road was privately destroying national currency and melting it into silver ingots. Chief Shen immediately dispatched Inspector Hong Wensun, leading Police Chief Mu Zhenjiang and other officers, to the scene. They apprehended Wu Ruisheng, a Jiangxi native, his wife Wan Wu, and two furnace workers. They also seized six silver ingots (each weighing approximately 50 taels), one ingot mold, 13 various account books, three checkbooks, and two check stubs. All were taken to the precinct for investigation.

During interrogation by Chief Shen, Wu Ruisheng confessed, "We are the old hands at the sand shop. Wu Yu Ji has gone to another port to solicit business. These ingots are not from the private destruction of national currency for profit. They were entrusted by Juxing Silver Shop on Avenue Edward VII to be melted for the making of silver ornaments." The Chief questioned the origin of the ingot mold, to which he replied, "Old Wu used to run a silver furnace but was ordered to close it." Considering the case involved the private destruction of national currency and recasting into silver ingots, it was deemed necessary to detain them pending investigation and to summon witnesses for further verification.

Cold Weather During Qingming Festival Leads to Many Illnesses

Crops Grow Very Slowly

Recently, the weather has been erratic, alternating between cold and hot, leading to a rise in cases of smallpox and scarlet fever among residents of this city. Yesterday, the 5th (Qingming Day), the weather suddenly changed from early morning, starting with drizzling rain followed by dark clouds and a piercing chill, making it unusually cold. With Qingming already past, such cold weather has caused crops in the rural fields to grow very slowly. As the Shanghai saying goes, "During Qingming in the second month, wheat grows evenly; during Qingming in the third month, wheat does not grow." This year, Qingming fell in the second month, but the wheat has still not grown evenly.

Dispute Over Rent in Xi Hua Li, Gongping Fang

Xi Hua Li, Gongping Fang, located in a remote part of the Eastern District, are both properties of Fuyuan Real Estate Company. Monthly rent for single-unit houses is as high as 60 taels, and for two-story houses, it reaches 37 yuan. Since the January 28th Incident, the market has been sluggish, and tenants are unable to bear the burden. Slightly overdue rent situations have occurred, and lawsuits have been filed once, but ended in reconciliation. According to the reconciliation agreement, tenants who were one or two months behind in rent were suddenly sued again by the landlord, who also requested the court to execute a preliminary attachment. Tenants did not receive prior warning, leading to the forced closure of several businesses, including Fufeng Rice Shop. The city-wide rent reduction movement is progressing to revive the market, but the tenants in that neighborhood are instead being subjected to pressure. They have strengthened their unity to seek a reasonable solution.

On the afternoon of the 26th of last month, at 3:45 PM, Public Concession Drug Squad Chinese Detective Zheng Huali and Western Inspector Bai Pu, raided a red pill manufacturing operation at No. 17 Nan Chang'an Lane, Wusong Road. They arrested Yong woman Yang Erxiang and her fellow villager Wang Liding, along with tens of thousands of red pills, a large package of white powder, machinery, and other items. All were taken to the Hongkou Police Station and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan continued the hearing in the Third Criminal Court. Attorney Wang Yaotang of the Public Works Department stated that further investigation revealed that defendant Wang Libao and the fugitive Li Atang were shareholders. Yang Tuxiang was sewing the red pill bags. The seized white powder was tested by the Public Works Department laboratory and found to be half heroin. The landlord of the house, Shi Su, is in court and can testify that the monthly rent of 30 yuan was originally rented by Wang Libao. The police are prosecuting the case under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law and request a severe penalty. Various exhibits were presented for inspection, and after Shi Su testified, the two defendants gave conflicting testimonies. Miscellaneous News

Yan Fusun Recruits Apprentices: Novelist Yan Fusun of Tongxiang is a champion of the literary world, a nephew of the reclusive writer, and is comparable to the greater and lesser Ruan brothers. In addition to writing, Fusun uses artistic techniques to invent [Gourd Divination], which is universally acclaimed for its judgments of people and affairs. It reveals the mysteries of Cangjie's creation of characters without leaving anything out. His wit and humor are unparalleled. With nine years of studying, he is recognized as the contemporary master. Now, as his writing work is increasing daily and his energy is declining, he urgently wants to pass on his knowledge and share the burden. He is soliciting the public. On the basis of artistic openness, he is recruiting five direct disciples to assist in the management of the library after they become proficient. Those who are interested, regardless of gender or age, will be registered and taught by correspondence methods for six months, followed by three months of practical training at the library. The treatment is favorable. After the internship is over, they will be allowed to set up their own studios, hang signs, and enter the world, or stay in the library to assist in writing, with monthly compensation determined by their performance. The tuition fee is 50 yuan, plus 5 yuan for correspondence expenses. Scholars from other ports can also apply. Yan's Gourd Wenjintin Pavillon is still located in the New World Hotel at the Shanghai Racecourse.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that in northeastern China and Shandong, the sky will be clear and gradually cloudy, with variable winds, due to a low-pressure system passing through Mongolia and moving eastward. In the Yangtze River Basin, including this area and the coastal area south of Ma'anshan Island, the sky will be overcast with drizzle, and there will be thin fog in several places. The wind will come from the northeast to the southeast. The Ryukyu Islands will experience cyclones and rain due to a small low-pressure system passing through and moving northeast-eastward. Furthermore, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city reached a high of 49.8 and a low of 44.4. On the same day last year, the high was 65.3 and the low was 41.7.

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor:

Regarding the news item in the Society section of your newspaper on March 28th, titled "Poochow Military Academy Fifth Term Graduate Yao Xijun Impersonates Teacher and Abuses Authority to Issue Orders," after investigation, there is no such person as Yao Xijun among the graduates of the Fifth Term of our school, nor is there anyone with the same name as the perpetrator in any term. It is evident that the perpetrator is using the name of a graduate of our school to impersonate a military officer and commit crimes. In addition to sending a separate letter to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters requesting severe punishment for the perpetrator, we hereby specially request your newspaper to promptly make a correction to avoid misleading the public and affecting the reputation of our school.

Respectfully,

Graduates Investigation Department, Central Military Academy

April 3rd

Having just read the news item published in your newspaper on the 5th of this month regarding the arrest of two more sanitation workers in western Shanghai yesterday, there are many discrepancies with the facts. Upon investigation, at around 3:00 AM yesterday morning (the 4th), officers from the Caojiadu Wujiaochang station brought in two sanitation workers, Jin Linsheng and He Yongfa, for allegedly spilling manure on the road, obstructing public sanitation. After interrogation by our district office, it was clarified that the manure workers claimed the manure cart had a crack, causing the manure to leak out, and they did not intentionally spill manure on the road. They were reprimanded and released, the manure cart was returned, and they were instructed to immediately repair the crack in the manure cart to prevent manure leakage and obstruction of hygiene. However, there was no arrest or detention of the manure workers.

We hereby inform you accordingly, hoping for a correction.

Respectfully,

Sixth District Office, Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau

Literary Column

Imperial Incense: Hazy Records

— Translated by Qin Shouou

Behind this palanquin, there were also six large sedan chairs, all painted red, each carried by eight eunuchs. These were for the attendant female officials, of which my sister Rongling and I were two.

The orderly procession advanced in an atmosphere of extreme solemnity. People and horses rarely made any noise. Occasionally, there was a cracking sound, which was the sound of the heavy sedan chair poles turning on the shoulders of the carriers. Apart from that, only the world-renowned chief eunuch Li Lianying would move around, shouting orders in a low but extremely fierce voice to the people in the procession. Because these ceremonial guards and processions were all arranged by him alone, everyone had to obey the orders of this terrifying demon.

From the gate of the Summer Palace to the gate of the Rehe Imperial Palace, on this official road, hundreds of miles long, the ground was covered with golden, damp yellow sand. Ordinary people were not only forbidden to walk on this imperial road, but were also to be executed if they were caught standing in the distance, gazing at the imperial carriage passing by. Therefore, no one had ever dared to violate this rule.

The procession moved on and on. This yellow snake-like imperial road gradually wound its way into the verdant valleys. We secretly wondered what kind of thoughts the Empress Dowager was having at this moment? She had been away from Rehe for almost fifty years. That place could be considered her birthplace. At that time, she was a very beautiful and young woman. Her position in the palace was only that of a favored concubine of Emperor Xianfeng. Because Xianfeng died suddenly, it immediately stirred up the conspiracy of two powerful ministers in the court, who wanted to depose her young son - Tongzhi - and usurp his throne.

Although she was not very familiar with the situation in the court at that time, and she did not have any special experience, the environment forced her to use a very clever strategy to deal with those two conspirators - Yixuan and Sushun. Later, with a heart full of worry, she snatched her son from the tiger's mouth, and on this yellow snake-like imperial road, fled from Rehe back to Beijing. (4)

How to Converse?

— Shen Minxing

A person who is good at conversation, who uses beautiful words and humorous tones to arouse the hearing of others, and to make others admire him, will surely gain many advantages in his life.

Therefore, a person who is good at conversation can not only make strangers like him when they meet him, but also make and get to know many friends. Taking "a person must have friends," "friends are our good teachers," and "relying on friends when away from home" as proof, then a person who is good at conversation can gain even greater advantages.

The refinement or crudeness, the excellence or inferiority of conversation, is most sufficient to show your level of education and your status. Your words will often unintentionally reveal the events of your life. Your conversation will announce all your secrets and reveal your true face to the world.

We often see people who have ideas in their hearts, but their words are not sufficient to express them; who want to speak, but stutter and cannot speak. These people can be considered the most pitiful people in the world!

Some people have brilliant thoughts and unique opinions, but they cannot express them. Their language is not sufficient to make their thoughts look like something. Their words are like a revolving lantern, always the same set of words. I ask, what effect do such people have on society?

On the contrary, does society need such people?

The American educator Eliot once said: "In the education that creates an 'upper-class person,' there is one training that cannot be missing: elegant and refined conversation."

Therefore, the art of conversation is a practical need, a need that cannot be missing!

Under the Rain

— Shang Wen

The rain began to fall softly at dawn, but it was very light; and the air became unusually dull. It seemed misty, everything was blurred, and everything was stained with a layer of water vapor, damp.

By noon, the rain had become very heavy! The sky seemed much lower than usual, and the air became even more oppressive. Terrible weather, not a breath of wind, stifling!

Under the rain: I thought of my umbrella, I thought of my sister with the umbrella, my sister who had been with me under the umbrella for three years!

Nine years ago, my sister loved me then, and she had not passed away. Under the rain, we held up an umbrella. The umbrella belonged to both of us, and we bought it together in Hangzhou.

The rain was still falling, and our umbrella, which was once a vibrant green, had faded to a pale white, already nine years old. My sister, too, has been dead for three years!

The rain is falling even harder today, hitting my body and imprinting itself on my heart. The umbrella is lost, under the rain, I walk with hurried, disordered steps, and two lines of tears flow straight down from my eyes, beaten down by the raindrops!

The Great Republic of China

Northeast Fourth Company Commander

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 27: The Grievances of Fujian Province Subside in Secret, Kind Hearts are Moved; Idle Sorrows Arise after Drunkenness, Old Affairs are Hard to Forget

Yang Guizhi was imagining ways to pass the time in bed that night, and naturally she couldn't help but think about the future. But as soon as she thought about the future, she remembered the many precedents on this Haidian Street. Some were middle-aged women left behind by their husbands who had died in battle, raising young children. Others were old mothers left behind when their sons went out and never returned, waiting at home every day. If she were to say that she might not end up like that, it was possible. Then there was Huang Manying, who would never be like that, because she was basically a woman without a master, and her relationship with Company Commander Tian was just that of friends. There was no need to ask about Tian Qing's future, because even as things stood now, it would not be illegal for her to marry someone. So she was very free, caring little about her family or friends, and openly dating a boyfriend. When I saw her boyfriend at the time, I was very embarrassed for her. But she didn't care at all, and even introduced him to me, saying that he was her cousin. These days, it turns out that love between men and women is like this: they are together, intimate, wishing they could become one person. But when they turn around, they each go and find their own lover. And me? I originally had a lover, Gan Erye. But I am very loyal to my husband, and after I got engaged to him, I didn't share any of my thoughts with Gan, and he probably knew that I wasn't of two minds, so he absolutely didn't come to tease me. If he did come to tease me, could I be like Huang Manying, treating him like a cousin and inviting him home to chat? Guizhi kept turning the event she had seen at Huang's house during the day over and over in her mind, thinking about it, and in the end, the key point was still that other people were not married, while she was married. How could she have the same freedom as others? (355)

Chatter

Research on Inkstones (17)

— A Bored Guest

General Overview of She Inkstones

(4) The information provided in the previous section on inkstone pits is just a general overview. Now, I will record the famous pits separately as follows:

(1) Longwei Mountain is located in the southeast of Wuyuan County, about fifteen miles away. It is connected to Wu Creek in the west. The mountains are picturesque and the water is clear. All the other mountains are branches of Longwei Mountain, extending for over a hundred miles. This pit was opened during the Southern Tang Dynasty and abandoned during the Northern Song Dynasty.

(2) Luowen Mountain, also known as Furong Creek, has more than ten interconnected pits along the creek. There are no stones in the creek. Some enthusiasts have passed down the story that they are called stones in the water. It is said that the old pit of Luowen is located in Zaitou, which is where Qian Xianzhe of the Northern Song Dynasty's Jingyou era visited the old stone quarry of the Southern Tang Dynasty. The color of the upper pit is slightly heavier, the color of the middle pit is slightly lighter, and the lower pit is the mudstone.

(3) Meizi Pit is located to the west of Luowen Mountain. From the creek to the pit is more than ten feet. The pit has no soil, and it is more than ten feet deep and two or three feet wide. It was discovered during the Kaiyuan era.

(4) Jinxing Pit is located to the northwest of Luowen Mountain. There are very few high-quality stones, and most are rough and sparse.

(5) Bili Pit is located in Jiyuan. The color of the stone is green and translucent. Within half a mile, there are Shuibu stones and Dadudian stones. Ten miles away, there are Qingshan stones, which are fine and green with golden patterns and halo-like markings, varying in shape.

(6) Shuixuan Pit is located outside the Mei Pit. It can be accessed when it is dry in winter. The stones are found at a depth of more than ten feet and often have golden flower eyebrow markings.

(7) Shui Jue Pit is located to the northwest of Luowen Mountain. It was discovered during the Jingyou era. The stones have wave-like patterns, but they are no longer available today.

(8) Xitou Pit is located to the north of Jinxing Pit. The Jinxing stones are flawed and slow to ink.

(9) Ye Jiu Pit is located to the west of Xitou Pit. It has eyebrow stones, which are slightly rough and slow to ink.

(10) Lu Pit is located to the northwest of the county. During the Jingyou era, the magistrate Cao Ping extracted stones from it. The guard Wang Junyu also extracted stones from it. During the Jiayou era, the lieutenant Diao Qiu extracted stones from it. The stones have a blue-green halo, but they are no longer produced.

(11) Jiyuan Pit, Bili Shuibu, these three pits are adjacent to each other. (The Shuibu stones with raindrop-like white halos are the "Shuasi Luowen" mentioned in Lu Shen's Chunfengtang Collection of Books).

(12) Lingyan Mountain has three interconnected caves. The raw stones have few flaws, dry slowly, and the lustrous ones resemble Duanxi stones.

(13) Hidden within the Ma stones are inkstone materials that are several inches long, like jade in the rough, found in the streams and can be collected when they are dry in winter.

According to Gao Sisun's Inkstone Notes, the above-mentioned pits are credible. However, according to other books, there are also Jinzu, Zhuangji, and Yu pits listed alongside the Luowen Pit. Their stones are inferior to those of the old pit. Mudstone, Zao Xin, and Green Stone are three pits located next to the old pit. The mudstone is warm, smooth, and dense, but not very firm. The fine Zao Xin stones are warm and lovely, with small patches of roughness and slight dryness. Green Stone is slightly tender in texture, and those with Luowen markings are the best. The Shuibo Pit is close to the lower pit of Luowen and produces Guazi Luowen, which is rare. However, due to the long passage of time, the pit veins are no longer known. The Miaoqian Pit is located in front of the ancient temple on Luowen Mountain, and it is as moist as purple jade with gold star speckles. One or two were discovered during the Jingyou era of the Song Dynasty, but their location has since been lost.

The conditions of the pits are generally as described above, but the famous materials are often found in deep streams. One must wait until the water is dry in winter and gather dozens of workers to excavate. If it rains even once, the previous work is all abandoned. The difficulty of mining is no less than that of the Lower Rock of Duanxi. Moreover, after the Song Dynasty, all the old pits were abandoned, and famous materials are no longer produced. Unlike Duan inkstones, which continue to be discovered, She inkstones that are truly good ones from the old pits are even more valuable today.

Overseas Chinese in the Philippines Firmly Oppose the Puppet State's Attempt to Participate in the Far Eastern Games

The Chamber of Commerce Convenes Responsible Organizations from Various Schools and Groups

Gathering the Strength of All to Make a Final Effort with Effective Methods

A Telegram Sent to the Shanghai Press Association Yesterday

Since Japan proposed that the puppet state of Manchuria participate in the upcoming Far Eastern Games, the voices of opposition from overseas Chinese in Manila have been very strong. Although our government has repeatedly expressed its attitude, firmly rejecting the puppet state's participation, the voices of opposition continue unabated. Our newspaper received another telegram yesterday from overseas Chinese in Manila to the Shanghai Press Association, stating that the Chinese Chamber of Commerce had convened various overseas Chinese newspapers, schools, and public organizations throughout the Philippines to form a support association to make a vigorous opposition and resolutely reject the participation of the puppet state of Manchuria. The original telegram is as follows:

"[To] the Shanghai Shenbao and the Journalists' Association: Yesterday, the Manila Overseas Chinese Commercial Daily, New China Daily, News Daily, Pioneer Daily, and Minzhong Journal jointly requested the Chinese Chamber of Commerce to convene various groups, schools, and newspapers to organize an agency to deal with the puppet state's participation in the Games, suggesting three points: (1) The Chamber of Commerce should convene various chambers of commerce, the All-Philippines Salvation Federation, the National Crisis Support Association, various groups, schools, and newspapers to organize a responsible agency to address this issue. (2) In the name of the responsible agency, send telegrams to China and abroad to awaken the public to unanimously oppose the puppet state's participation in the Far Eastern Games, and issue documents to promote it abroad, so that people of all countries can know the true public opinion of our country. (3) If our country's sports association authorities, under the military pressure of the political environment, generously allow the puppet state to participate at the round table conference, then this responsible agency should gather the strength of all to make a final effort with effective methods, such as sending telegrams to various provinces in our country to dissuade athletes from participating. If there are those who are willing to be slaves of a subjugated nation and dare to attend, they should be condemned by all, and urge overseas Chinese to unanimously boycott the Games and not enter the venue. Today, the Chinese Chamber of Commerce has decided to fully accept it, and scheduled a general meeting on the ninth to discuss the implementation plan. Please publicize it widely. Sincerely, Pioneer Daily, Kouchi]"

There are a total of thirteen teams participating in this competition, with Chinese accounting for six teams, including the Jingwu Sports Association, the China Sports Association (two teams), the Huaguang Track and Field Team, and the Feima Hongkou Two Cross-Country Team. The strongest in this competition should be the French Army, the British Army, and the Russian Overseas Chinese Team. There will be a fierce battle for the championship. The Chinese are not without capable players, but they are scattered among the teams. Although Jingwu has famous Shanghai players such as Chen Xuzhou, Wang Zhenglin, and Zhou Ruquan, the hope for the championship is very slim. Jin Zhongkang, who won the first place in the 10,000-meter demonstration at the National Games, has also joined the competition. However, he rarely practices at the venue. This kind of muddy road track requires sufficient experience to cope with, so it is still a question whether Jin can win the championship. In short, the Chinese have completely given up hope in this competition. The names of each team are listed below:

Soviet Union Expands Compulsory Education

Huge Educational Expenditure in Five Years

- 19.5 Billion Rubles

(Moscow Correspondence) The increase in educational expenditure in the past three years has been very significant. This increase is in pursuit of the popularization of compulsory education. In 1913, the educational expenditure per person in Russia was 1.73 rubles, while in the Soviet Union in 1932, it was 38.54 rubles. The total amount of funds used for the national economy in the past five years reached 19.5 billion rubles. In standard cities such as Ropinsk, the number of students in schools was 3,215 in 1915, 5,250 in 1928, and 12,500 in 1933. The city now has various educational institutions such as an aviation research institute, a normal night school, two workers' schools, six factory schools, ten ordinary night schools, ten primary schools, ten kindergartens, two libraries, and several ordinary junior and grammar schools. A few years ago, the proportion of workers' children in the lower grades was very high, while in the higher grades, it was very low. Now, there is no such difference in their proportion.

Zhejiang Department of Education Orders and Promulgates Measures for Holiday Assignments in Vocational Schools

The Zhejiang Department of Education believes that holiday assignments are of great help to the academic work of students in vocational schools. Based on the regulations for vocational schools promulgated by the Ministry of Education and with reference to the actual situation in the province, it has drafted a set of measures for holiday assignments in vocational schools in Zhejiang Province. It has been submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and ordered to be followed by all vocational schools. The measures are recorded below:

Measures for Holiday Assignments in Vocational Schools in Zhejiang Province

1. Holiday assignments for students in vocational schools in this province (hereinafter referred to as holiday assignments) shall be handled in accordance with these measures.

2. Holiday assignments are divided into summer holiday assignments, winter holiday assignments, and spring holiday assignments. Schools may suspend giving holidays or change the implementation of holidays in accordance with the regulations for vocational schools and with reference to the actual situation.

3. Holiday assignments may be carried out on or off campus, as designated by the school in accordance with the nature of the assignment.

4. Regardless of whether the holiday assignment is on or off campus, the school should formulate a holiday assignment plan and report it to the Department of Education for record before the holiday begins.

5. The holiday assignment plan should include the following purposes: (1) mastering skills, (2) expanding practical knowledge, (3) strengthening physique and developing labor habits, (4) cultivating necessary qualities related to the profession, (5) understanding the actual situation of the profession, (6) real-time communication with the vocational industry.

6. The holiday assignment plan should specify the working methods, work procedures, and the amount of work to be assigned. However, for off-campus holiday assignments where students are sent to other institutions for internships, only an outline may be specified, and the details of the work shall be negotiated separately between the school and the internship institution.

7. Students should follow the instructions specified in the holiday assignment plan issued by the school, work in order, and submit a report (with a diary) on the progress of the assignment to the school immediately after the completion of the holiday assignment.

8. The student's holiday assignment report should be evaluated by the original teacher and used as an important part of the daily practice grade.

9. Students' holiday assignments on campus should be discussed by the original teacher to provide guidance and examine the results at any time.

10. For off-campus holiday assignments, whether in agriculture, the school should contact off-campus farms or other agricultural institutions; in industry, the school should contact off-campus factories or other industrial institutions; in commerce, the school should contact off-campus banks, shops, or other institutions related to commerce before the holiday in order to dispatch students for internships as scheduled. The supervising officers of the respective institutions may be consulted to guide the students during these internships. When necessary, the original teacher should also supervise and provide guidance.

11. All measures for holiday assignments should still be handled in accordance with the Ministry-approved standards for student internships in vocational schools.

12. These measures are formulated by the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education and will be promulgated and implemented after being submitted to the Ministry of Education and the Provincial Government for record.
