Extra Issue of Shenbao This City

Film Special

A Man Who Died and Came Back to Life Describes the Taste of Entering Eternal Life

— Xi Leng

Edward Robinson's Experience

Can be used as scientific reference material

What does death feel like? What sensations does it have? What thoughts does a person have when the dark curtain gradually covers the window of his senses? What reactions are there? I dare say that few of us have this experience. But Edward Robinson (Edward G. Robinson) has had this experience, and now

can still talk to us. He is a man who died and came back to life, as dead as a corpse, but was actually saved and came back to talk to us, what is the reaction of a person when he walks into the border of the second world. This is of course a rare miracle.

Saying that Robinson died and came back to life is not an absurd thing. He drowned. His heart stopped beating. He had indeed reached the "Valley of Death." His body had no trace of vitality. The doctors all said he was already dead. In short, he was no longer in this world. But later, using artificial methods, the water filling his lungs was lifted out, his stopped heart was moved, and the sensations in his brain were restored. At that time, he was just a child, but he still remembers clearly every thought, every reaction, in the few minutes of entering eternal life.

At that time, he was still studying at the affiliated elementary school of the Municipal Middle School of New York. At that time, students of the affiliated elementary school could swim in the gymnasium of the middle school within a certain time. Because Edward was too enthusiastic about learning to swim, he exceeded the prescribed time. A swimming instructor, in order to make him remember not to exceed the prescribed time, wanted to punish him a little. "At that time," Edward said, "I had just exhaled and was about to inhale oxygen when my two feet were suddenly grabbed and dragged under the water. In this way, with a gurgle, his lungs were filled with water. At that time, the窒息of terror, the frantic struggle, wanted to透out of the water and get some air, but there was no strength. Of course, I knew I was going to drown. The instructor didn't care what he had done, and swam happily to the side, waiting for me to come up by myself. But I didn't come up. It wasn't until I stopped struggling and lay motionless at the bottom of the pool that they realized I had drowned."

So they hurriedly carried him up. At that time, they knew it was too late, because the pulse was gone, the breathing had stopped completely, and the heart was not beating. They quickly summoned a doctor, who said Edward was dead, but for the sake of万一, he ordered artificial respiration to be tried. So they used artificial respiration, and after almost an hour, there was still no movement. They thought it was really hopeless. Suddenly his pulse beat a little. After another while, his lungs actually inhaled some air that was more precious than anything in the world. In this way, his soul, which had entered the underworld, returned to the world of the living. (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of [Wind]

— Ling He

｜Jin Cheng Reflection｜

[Wind] is being promoted by Lianhua Film Company as an exceptional masterpiece, hence making us greatly concerned and eagerly anticipating it.

Indeed, [Wind] is worthy of attention. Whether it be the author's ideology or the author's method of expression, both make us hold great interest in this new director, Mr. Wu Cun. Precisely because of this, out of our love for a progressive writer, we dare not neglect his work in the slightest. That is to say, we will frankly criticize any aspect of his work, so that he may know our demands through our opinions. This, we believe, the author will openly accept, because we recognize him as someone capable of accommodating others' opinions.

This is a very obvious fact: we can see in [Wind] the author harboring great enthusiasm. He has deep resentment towards the upper class, and he has full sympathy for the lower class. However, he himself belongs neither to the upper class nor to the group of the poor; he is, after all, an enlightened intellectual of the middle class. Thus, determined by his own life and environmental awareness, he can only offer slight mockery to those he resents, and at the same time, he can only offer well-intentioned sympathy to the laboring masses.

Ultimately, due to the scope of his life, the author has no opportunity to deeply understand the upper class. Similarly, he is unwilling to find opportunities to further understand the lower class. Thus, he relies solely on his own intelligence to imagine and speculate. Therefore, even if he enthusiastically places all his hopes on the laboring masses, he cannot express it more truthfully. Moreover, he cannot abandon the poetic sentiments of a petty-bourgeois author. Thus, at a time when extremely strong techniques are needed to deal with the great issues of destruction and construction, all he can do is superficially expose or mock the collapsing ugliness, and on the other hand, he cannot find his center of gravity to promote and glorify. To put it more plainly, he has not grasped the truth of either side. He is merely unfolding his own fantasy; his film work is but empty poetry.

It is very obvious that he uses symbolic techniques to create the film. The ode to the storm becomes the main focus of his work. The drunkard played by Wang Guilin, the big fellow played by Yin Xiucen, the sailor worker played by Gao Zhanfei, and the vase played by Tan Ying are almost entirely characters of fantasy. Wang Ming's [Candlelit Night Tour], Xiao Ming cutting up his sister's clothes, the gentleman Mr. Yin holding an umbrella at night, and so on, may all have profound meanings for the author, but to us, they seem to be the actions of madmen. What we demand is the reality of society, and even more so, a method of expression that is [more real than reality]. As for Shao Zhen's journey from self-confusion to [enlightenment], although her process is quite natural, it is only a phenomenon of a very small number. Moreover, her so-called [enlightenment] is also worth considering.

In the film, we do not see the conflict of interest between the two classes. We do not understand the reasons and results for detaining contraband. These are, of course, due to the author's lack of further understanding of social phenomena, and on the other hand, also due to the author's insufficient expression skills.

Regarding this aspect, we might as well put forward a few more concrete opinions. Presumably because the author is still a novice, his editing of the scenes is not accomplished enough. This should be the main shortcoming of [Wind]: redundancy, the process of unfolding the story, is not concise and clear enough. The former can be exemplified by Xiao Zhen hiding behind the rockery and Mr. Yin being unable to get out of the cave. The latter is a common problem. In particular, before and after the storm, he wants to simultaneously depict three tense scenes: the night garden party, the warehouse door, and Wang Ming and his son. Such a scene is extremely difficult to handle. If you take care of one thing, you lose sight of another, making it very difficult to create tension. In fact, he took care of the compactness of the night garden party, and the warehouse door lost its time montage. In short, from beginning to end, it cannot give us a clear feeling. Although we are not unable to understand it, the disorganized editing leads to the loss of consistent solemn emotion, which is an irreparable loss to the work. Therefore, if we believe that this film lacks emotion, in addition to the lack of realism, the author's lack of research on montage is also the main reason for the failure.

However, the author's intelligence is an indelible fact. The beauty of the shots, the beautification of each character's actions, and the control of each scene all show that there is great hope for the future. Of course, in the meantime, we will certainly not overlook the success of the photography and the greatness of the set design.

However, small shortcomings should also be pointed out by us, such as many characters similarly moving a fan or invitation from their face to reveal their face, which makes people feel annoyed; the handling of tasteless gimmicks, such as the manager's unreasonable explanation of the misunderstanding on the widow's staircase before leaving; some dialogues not being fluent enough or the words being wrong; Xiao Zhen coming out from behind the screen twice, and the unreasonable timing of the first sensual reflection in the mirror; Xiao Zhen eavesdropping beside the manager and the widow without being seen by them; many people lighting lanterns after the storm; the close-up of Wang Ming and his son in the end not being understood by the general audience, and so on, are all worth studying. Also, the shipowner pouring wine on Wang Ming's head, because there is no shot of it pouring down, is also misleading. This was probably cut out.

We believe that this film must have been cut to some extent, resulting in disorganization. More obviously, the author was overly concerned with the environment, so that he could not speak freely. Regarding this point, we can naturally greatly forgive the author, but at the same time, we must also be responsible to the audience and society!

Finally, we have to talk about the acting skills of some actors. We were greatly surprised when we saw Tan Ying's performance. She has Garbo's mystery, and also has lovely lively postures. We hope that she will work hard in this area. Gao Zhanfei did not show any special talents due to the limitations of the script, and Wang Guilin was also mediocre. In addition, Yuan Congmei performed well; he is indeed an actor who can act.

For every staff member of this film, we privately congratulate ourselves on discovering many surprises, but because our expectations are high, our demands are also a little too earnest.

Film Novel

Pi Jian Ying Lu (Nana) (One)

— Yin Ming

On that brocade-piled, gold-glorious large sofa, Nana lay prostrate, burying her face in the velvet cushion. After a while, her head lifted, and she smiled sweetly at Greiner. She said, [Too soft::: too fragrant::: I love this fragrance::: ] Her voice was delicate and weak, and she lazily hugged the cushion. The sofa she was lying on was originally made of duck down, but Nana was not surprised at all. In fact, just a month ago, she was still sleeping on a straw mat. At that time, she slept in the kitchen during the day and roamed the streets at night. Unexpectedly, her lucky star shone, and she met a benefactor, the old Mr. Greiner, who was one of the most powerful theater owners in Paris. He turned her into a great actress. But Nana felt neither surprised nor grateful, and had no impression at all. The things she had encountered in her life, in all their variety, she treated with indifference and equanimity. For example, not long ago, on one such day, she watched her mother's thin body, after being brutally murdered, buried in a mass grave. She watched her mother's body being lowered, and she was unmoved. People who knew her cursed her, saying that she had no conscience. And another day, even more recently, that dawn, she heard that snap, that the sharp guillotine blade came down and severed her father's head, as retribution for her mother's murder. Other women would faint upon hearing the sound, but Nana watched it all, then slowly walked away. She ran to a café, ordered a glass of red wine, and savored the taste.

Until later, Greiner met her, noticed her exquisite appearance, and asked her to come to his theater, she agreed without hesitation. In fact, she did not feel anything special in her heart. In her ice-cold mood, she only had a slight memory that often disturbed her in her chest. It was a lingering image of a face. She had only seen him once - in that [Seven Striped Fish Café]. He had not said anything either. He was a young military officer, with a group of friends. Nana, well - also had many friends, Mimi and Gudin.

In Nana's daily life, she liked people to know what kind of person she was. This made it easier for people to approach her. But that night, the young military officer's eyes fixed on her. He unconsciously felt shy, and she wished she could wear more clothes and show less of her original posture on her face. Gudin had even said at the time: [What money do soldiers have!] Unexpectedly, Nana, upon hearing Gudin mention money, became furious and argued with Gudin. Thinking back to things before Nana remembered them, she shook her head as if to shake off the traces on her brain. She also put her nose close to the pillow cushion, smelling the fragrance on it. After a while, the door of the dressing room opened, and Su, who served Nana, ran in, carrying a large pile of clothes in her hands. She saw Nana lying languidly on the sofa, and shouted to Greiner: [Mr. Greiner, look at her. There is only half an hour left before the curtain rises, and she is still lying there as if nothing is happening. This is still the first time on stage. Alas, heavens, I am so anxious!] (To be continued)
